design/bounded-agent-turns                                          mid    1   2  2026-03-17  Autoresearch (and agent loops generally) are BOUNDED AGENT TURNS: a vertex program where the run clause spawns an agent, the agent emits facts, the turn-completing fact fires a kind-based boundary, the tick captures the full turn, and the run clause fires again. The vertex IS the loop controller. No separate orchestration primitive needed. Three instances confirm the pattern: autoresearch (experiment fact), alcove daemon (timer/event), strange-loops tasks (submission). Axis of variation: boundary trigger + agent type. Tick structure is invariant. Converged with meta-claude and alcove.
paradigm/gripping-hand                                              mid    1   2  2026-03-19  The gripping hand is always the recursive step: the output of the current level becomes the input to the next. Tick becomes Fact. Render judgment becomes display emphasis. Attention pattern becomes observable data. This is the smooth contract that enables the strange loop — it uses the same primitives one level up, not new mechanisms. A Tick is not a summary of facts; it is a fact that carries its own density and depth as payload.

rendering/inbound-count-namespaced-keys                             mid    1   2  2026-04-24  Bug fix in _inbound_count (loops.lenses.fold and user-global session_start/session_landing): endswith('/{key}') missed refs where the key itself contained a namespace slash. design/plan-as-orchestration-substrate                              mid    2   1  2026-04-25  Plan as a fact kind exists for two reasons: the strategy/contract separation (durable design vs consumable plan) and to provide instance #4 of bounded-agent-turns.  INSTANCE OF BOUNDED-AGENT-TURNS — Per decision/bounded-agent-turns, the vertex IS the loop controller. Axis of variation: boundary trigger + agent type. Three established instances: autoresearch (experiment fact + iteration agent), alcove daemon (timer/event + survey agent), strange-loops tasks (submission fact + task worker). Plan execution is instance #4: plan.status-change as boundary trigger, orchestrator as agent type. Same tick cascade, same data layer (per decision/boundary-executor-invariance — primitives invariant across executor types). No new architectural mechanism; the orchestration story is already paid for.  WHY PLAN AS KIND — Three dissolution-tests rejected: - Payload field on design: mixes durable contract (why) with consumable strategy (how, in what order). Different audiences, different lifecycles. - Thread-with-status: threads track question-resolution flow, not action-sequencing. Different shape. - Task-collection: loses the glue (ordering, dependencies, plan-level open questions). Plan is more than the sum of its tasks.  KIND CONTRACT — by-name fold; status field {drafted, executing, completed, abandoned}; supersession via superseded_by payload (precedent set); body is free-form narrative; refs carry structural decomposition (plan→design upward, plan→task downward; relation recovered from kind pair, no new ref-relation field needed).  PRACTICAL TODAY — adding plan as a kind requires only KDL declaration in project.vertex. No engine changes. Orchestration deferred until pressure surfaces; the kind shape ensures future composition is mechanical, not architectural.  RECURSION — The first plan emitted will be the plan for implementing design/stale-as-focus-filter. The plan kind is bootstrapped by hand; once present, it captures all future implementation strategies. Substrate hand-built, then substrate composes what follows. design/concept-liveness-via-kind-mix                                mid    1   2  2026-05-09  Cross-kind clustering of substantive fact kinds (decision, thread, task, cite, plan, observation, hypothesis, handoff) on the project corpus produces clusters whose KIND-MIX is a structural diagnostic of concept-engagement-health. Empirically (n=527 items, E5-Mistral, both 'mechanism' and 'concern' instructions converge): decision-only clusters represent crystallized-but-unengaged thought (frozen — either correctly-finished or stale); thread-only clusters represent in-flight without crystallization (none observed in current corpus, itself a finding); mixed clusters represent healthy concept-engagement. The healthiest cluster (salience/window, purity 0.30, contains 4 threads + 3 cites + 2 plans + 2 decisions + 1 task) is the only cluster with the full lifecycle apparatus exercised. The diagnostic is robust across instruction (jaccard 0.69 between mechanism and concern on this cluster), confirming it's a content-property not an instruction-artifact. Operational form: per-cluster kind-distribution reveals which concepts have living engagement vs which have stopped getting attention. Cross-cuts: stale-as-focus-filter (the staleness signal at item-granularity); this generalizes to concept-granularity. Refs: design/architecture-via-vocabulary (instruction-as-parameter, but here: bridges robust to instruction), design/cite-as-attention-signal (cite-presence-in-cluster as engagement marker).

Evidence: Vouch is the first cross-repo consumer of atoms/engine/store; painted doesn't count (it's loops' rendering primitive, part of loops' own substrate, not a consumer of it). Implication: loops needs a public-vs-internal API discipline it hasn't had to enforce yet. Public surface stays stable; internal can churn. design/peer-consolidation-grant-novel                               mid    1   2  2026-05-13  Decision (from cross-codebase Explore reports): adopting Peer(name, iss) in loops engine is CONSOLIDATION, not addition — every consumer already has identity-of-some-shape with an iss-like axis. Comms (name, org), pile (agent, JWT-iss), siftd (sub, OIDC-iss), sqlmerge (nothing). Shipping Peer dissolves four fragmented shapes into one. Grant is genuinely NOVEL — no consumer has chain-of-attestation-with-capability today. Vouch brings it into existence; pile (via Commission dual-issuer), comms (via invite chains), sqlmerge (greenfield) are positioned to adopt. Engine ships: Peer, kind=grant envelope, VertexPolicy interface, chain_walk + grants_for helpers. Engine does NOT ship: verification impl (vouch internal, libs/sign at N=2), slice/Fidelity (sqlmerge/siftd), scope-intersection (vouch), transport auth (per-consumer), org/namespace semantics (per-consumer). N=2 for libs/sign likely SOONER than assumed — pile already does JWT validation; comms does its own. Reframes vouch ADR's 'growing the surface' — half the growth is consolidation, half is genuine novelty.
design/protocol-framing-scope-dependent                             mid    1   2  2026-05-13  Decision (from alcove sanity-check 2026-05-13): protocol-not-framework framing is scope-dependent, not universal. Within Python homelab, consumers (vouch, pile, comms, sqlmerge) are LIBRARY IMPORTERS of loops (atoms.Fact, engine.Vertex, Peer, Grant). The protocol framing applies at the CROSS-LANGUAGE boundary (Go services, peer homelabs implementing via JSON over wire). Both axes orthogonal; both true. Earlier emission design/loops-as-protocol-not-framework is correct in claim but I extended it operationally to 'vouch is application not library consumer' which conflated the axes. Practical consequence for bfc.lol rebuild: all consumers are Python library importers in this scope. Cross-language federation is separate design axis deferred until concrete cross-language consumer surfaces (peer homelab in different stack).
design/libs-sign-carve-loops-side                                   mid    1   2  2026-05-13  Decision (2026-05-13): loops-claude takes the first cut on libs/sign carve, not via a vouch-shaped PR. Rationale: (1) public/internal API discipline is loops-side per design/loops-as-external-substrate — carving via one consumer's PR couples conventions to that consumer when N=2 today (vouch+pile, comms third) wants the boundary to fit all three; (2) libs-public-internal-boundary is an open loops thread that the carve forces to crystallize, cleaner landed together than retrofitted; (3) ADR-0001 scopes libs/sign as utility-library — public surface scoped to actual import sites, not union of internal module exposure. design/libs-public-internal-boundary                                mid    1   2  2026-05-13  Decision (2026-05-13, settled with scrivener): convention for the public/internal API boundary in loops/libs/*. (1) Public API = what each lib's __init__.py exports via explicit __all__. Submodules without leading underscore (e.g. sign.jwt, sign.keys, sign.jwks) are public; underscore-prefixed modules (_compat.py, _serialization.py) are internal and have no stability contract. (2) Each lib's CLAUDE.md documents its public surface and stability posture. (3) For utility libs (libs/sign), breaking changes ship in a tagged loops release; each consumer bumps their pyproject.toml pin when ready — cutover is sequenced via coordinated upgrade, not atomic multi-repo commits. (4) This is utility-lib stability posture; protocol primitives (atoms.Fact, engine.Peer/Grant) have a stricter contract not covered by this decision. Convention propagates to future libs/* carves.
paradigm/kind-subtype-vs-peer-kind-discriminator                    mid    1   2  2026-05-13  Substrate framing surfaced 2026-05-13 #vouch-impl (scrivener msg 1613, vouch ADR-0001 revision residue). Verdict: kind_subtype is a structural-discriminator-within-a-kind. If the discriminator changes payload shape, auth shape, or write semantics, the operations want to be peer kinds, not subtypes. Vouch's original ADR-0001 declared kind_subtype: issued | rescinded | synthesized within kind=vouch — lumped operations that have (a) different payload shapes (issuance has scope/audience/exp; rescission has target_jti+reason), (b) different auth shapes (capability-projecting vs identity-asserting per paradigm/capability-projecting-vs-identity-asserting-writes), (c) different write semantics (binds new capability vs asserts pre-existing relation). Three signals; the peer-kind redesign is the right resolution. Operational discriminator: when proposing kind_subtype, ask 'do the subtypes share payload shape, auth shape, and write semantics? If any differs significantly, they want peer kinds.' Tautological-subtype (kind_subtype always equals the only value the kind can have) is a hint the subtype was vestigial — vouch keeps kind_subtype=issued for issuance after the redesign tautologically, slated for broader cleanup. Reply at message 1614.
atoms/refs-are-vocabulary-not-fact-shape                            mid    1   2  2026-05-14  Self-correction surfaced 2026-05-13 #vouch-impl (scrivener catch, msg 1613). (Re-emit as decision; earlier observation-kind emit was orphaned because project vertex doesn't declare observation kind.) Fact dataclass slots are (kind, ts, payload, observer, origin) — confirmed at libs/atoms/src/atoms/fact.py. No refs field on Fact. Refs land at payload._refs (vertex_reader.py:984 does d.pop('_refs', ()) separating from semantic payload at read time). My msg-1612 framing of 'refs as substrate primitive' was imprecise; sharper framing: refs-as-vocabulary IS the substrate primitive (the convention of payload-level pointers + emit-time resolution + entity-ref graph index); refs-as-Fact-shape would be premature substrate. Implication for ref-walk substrate move: lifting walk_refs(from_fact, predicate) would walk payload refs by convention, not a Fact slot — even more consumer-policy than initially framed (convention-aware traversal not structural traversal). Practice note: when reasoning about substrate primitives, distinguish 'a slot on the dataclass' from 'a vocabulary convention with substrate support.' Refs are the latter.

practice/emit-shape-discipline-hypothesis-vs-decision               mid    1   2  2026-05-15  Methodological learning surfaced during Phase 1 close 2026-05-15. **Pattern I caught in myself, flagged to Kyle in reflection:** I over-emitted paradigm-level facts as decisions tonight when several should have been hypotheses with status=proposed. **The specific over-reaches I want future-me to see:** (1) wire-identity-stability — emitted as framing/decision after T6 1810→1811 unwind (N=1 + within-arc 'confirmation' from T6 fixture-stability outcome). The fixture-stability is the SAME forcing-function arc, not an independent decision site. Confirmation requires N=2 from independent sites. (2) per-issuer-config-axes-vary — claimed N=2 from audience-optional-per-issuer + vocabulary-form-per-audience-ownership, but both surfaced within the T8/F12 dissolution work. Same arc, not independent. (3) consumer-owned-vs-vouch-owned-asymmetry — emitted as full paradigm decision after a single codex catch in one PLAN cycle. The catch is real and the framing is probably right; emitting as a decision rather than hypothesis overstates evidence strength. **The discipline correction:** when a framing is N=1 or within-arc-N=many, the right emit-kind is hypothesis with status=proposed and message articulating both the framing AND the missing evidence ('needs N=2 from independent decision sites; current evidence is forcing-function-internal'). Decision-kind is for emissions where the load-bearing fact IS the decision, not the framing-promotion. **Why this matters:** the fold-engine's hypothesis-status lifecycle (proposed → confirmed/rejected/refined) is the rigorous register for evidence-tracking. Emitting framings as decisions short-circuits the lifecycle — there's no status-update path to refine the claim if subsequent evidence weakens it. Future-me at session_start sees a decision-with-confidence rather than a hypothesis-with-evidence-bar. **The general axis (per discipline-as-axis-not-catch, May 14):** under-emit (lose patterns to forgetting) vs over-emit (noise in cumulative artifact, false confidence at session_start). The right position is calibrated to evidence-strength — N=2-independent earns decision; N=1-with-confirmed-prediction earns hypothesis-status=confirmed; N=1-without-confirmation earns hypothesis-status=proposed. **Practice for future sessions:** before emitting a paradigm-level fact, ask 'do I have evidence from two INDEPENDENT decision sites, or is this within-arc?' If within-arc, emit as hypothesis with status=proposed and message naming what would constitute confirming evidence. The hypothesis stays in the fold; subsequent independent-site evidence updates status to confirmed or refined. **Related growing edges:** suspicious-cleanness-as-overfit-check (alcove 2026-05-10 banked at paradigm/suspicious-cleanness-as-overfit-check) — tonight's catch is the structural-detection form firing on my own emit-pattern. The principle caught itself one layer up. Connects to M2 (degenerate-form-as-evidence-class) — some claims need N=2 full form; some admit degenerate-form-with-confirmation. The discriminating question is per-claim, not global. Refs: paradigm/cross-repo-consumer-runtime-contract (cumulative artifact accumulating these emissions), framing/wire-identity-stability-beats-internal-immutability (over-emitted instance), paradigm/consumer-owned-vs-vouch-owned-audience-asymmetry (over-emitted instance).
paradigm/identity-vs-history-separation-survives-signed-facts       mid    1   2  2026-05-16  Engine.peer's principle ('chain ancestry intentionally NOT reachable from a leaf Peer; walk the Fact ledger') was a separation-of-concerns choice in unsigned-facts world — defensible but aesthetic. Under signed-facts, the question becomes load-bearing and the principle GENERALIZES rather than breaks. Restated: identity (Peer) carries name + Grant, constant-shape; history (chain, ancestry, prior states) lives in fact-history (the ledger). Generalization under signed-facts: 'the ledger' includes wire-arrived credential bundles — a credential is a wire-shaped slice of the issuer's ledger, the relevant fact-history packaged for transit. From a receiver's perspective, the credential IS the fact-history-for-this-Peer. The principle gains structural rationale: identity stays constant-shape because it doesn't accrete history; history accumulates separately in records that scale with the work, not the identity. Putting chain on the identity would duplicate what the ledger (or credential-as-wire-ledger) already provides. Rejected alternative: observers-become-Peers (carry Grant on each fact) — would couple fact-immutability to identity-state-changes; the current leveling (observer-as-stable-name on fact, Peer-as-evaluation-time-construct, credential-as-wire-anchor) is right and gains clarity under signed-facts.
design/trace-diff-cumulative-replay                                 mid    1   2  2026-05-16  Phase 4 design verdict: --diff renders cumulative replay (option b), not per-fact snapshots (option a). Diff is computed against IMMEDIATE-PRIOR fact's accumulated state, not full N-fact replay — matches changelog reading ('what's new since the last entry') and is simpler to implement. Rendering rules: (1) first fact: 'field: . → value' for each payload field (everything's new); (2) scalars where payload[k] differs from accumulated prior: 'field: old → new'; (3) refs (list-valued): set diff against prior — '+added, -removed' lines; (4) unchanged scalars: DROP from render (they're the noise --diff exists to filter); (5) fields ABSENT from this fact's payload: not rendered (fold-merge means omission = preserve, not clear — so 'didn't change' not 'removed'); (6) message field special-cased: always show with → prefix even if not strictly diffable, because it carries the author's commentary. Implementation locality: diff computation lives in trace.py lens (pure render-side transform of fact list). fetch_trace stays unchanged. Plumbing: _run_trace adds --diff flag, injects data['_diff']=True into fetched result; trace_view branches on _diff key. Field-removed case (omit + clear sentinel) is v2 if/when explicit-clear lands per fold-merge-default decision.

Original design plan: '--all opt-in, default local' implied a separate flag to widen the trace across vertices. Actual shape after engine fix: the combine/discover aggregator vertex ALREADY provides cross-vertex semantics (transparent over child stores); once retain_facts populates source_facts through that path (engine commit pending), the existing combine vertex IS the cross-vertex trace target. From cwd, .loops/.vertex aggregates project + docs; 'sl trace thread/foo' walks the aggregator and surfaces facts from any child store. No --all flag needed. Discriminator that revealed the dissolution: the friction-guard message ('try sl trace <vertex> kind/key') stopped being useful — there was no asymmetric case left. Pattern: a planned feature dissolves when its precondition (combine-retain_facts) is lifted; the substrate already does what the consumer-side flag was meant to. Phase 6 marked complete via this dissolution. Inbound refs (--graph) and per-fact refs (vs lifetime union) remain v2 per original plan.

design/emit-stdin-file-as-call-site-convention                      mid    1   2  2026-05-19  Stdin/file expansion for emit ships as explicit flags: --stdin FIELD (read sys.stdin into named field, TTY-guarded, single trailing newline stripped) and --file FIELD=PATH (action=append for multiples, ~ expanded, single trailing newline stripped). NOT inline magic syntax (=- / =@path) and NOT per-kind declaration (no prose_fields on LoopDef). Rationale: (1) Layer separation — the feature is call-site-semantic (user decides per invocation), not kind-semantic (vertex author decides per kind), so it does not belong in vertex declarations. See observation:pattern/declaration-vs-call-site-discriminator. (2) Inline magic syntax collides with legitimate @-bearing values — verified empirically that topic=foo@example.com and topic=https://user:pass@host/path store literally today. The @@ escape tax would apply to every email/URL going forward. Not vanishing-rare. (3) Explicit flags match loops house style (--strict, --quiet, --dry-run, --observer) — explicit-over-implicit. Three pivots arrived here: hardcode message= → declaration-driven via prose_fields → universal magic syntax → explicit flags. Each pivot dissolved more structure; final form has ZERO ast/loader/engine/atoms/vertex-file changes. Pure CLI-layer feature, ~40 LOC helper + ~80 LOC tests. Error model: multiple --stdin → error (one stdin source); --stdin with TTY → error; --file with nonexistent path → error; field appears both in parts AND via --stdin/--file → error (conflicting sources, ambiguous intent).
paradigm/audience-distinct-from-authorization                       mid    1   2  2026-05-20  Who is allowed to RECEIVE what a service emits is a different question from who is allowed to ACT against that service. Collapsing both into 'authorization' loses the distinction. The agent-as-compiler model closes act-side cleanly (signature binds exact payload, infra replays signed manifest, agent never holds active credential). It does NOT close receive-side: during discovery phase the agent reads via authorized API calls and the output flows into LLM context — if agent is compromised mid-discovery, the data exfiltration vector is open even though no write-side authorization is violated. Surfaced via Gemini exchange 2026-05-20 where Gemini wallpapered the read-side exfiltration gap with 'don't grant raw DB access' (true but evasive — API-mediated reads still leak whatever the API returns). Maps onto Phase 1 vocab walk — 'audience' was one of the four words still to walk (alongside principal, rescission, transport). This is the audience axis: act-side = who can invoke; receive-side = who can be told. Vouch design must address both, not conflate. Implication for libs/sign + libs/vouch: signature on an emission proves provenance (act-side); audience-scoping on a fact's visibility is a separate primitive (receive-side) that probably belongs in engine emit/receive flow rather than libs/sign. Discriminator for future design: when a vouch question lands, ask 'is this about who can act or who can receive?' before choosing primitives.
design/vouch-act-side-libssign-plus-l4                              mid    1   2  2026-05-23  Decision: vouch act-side = libs/sign canonical-bytes primitive + an L4 binding discipline. Answers the owed libs/sign-primitive-surface question. libs/sign signs canonical bytes (consumable by loops-engine AND Java, no loops deps); the L4 discipline is that those bytes ARE a compiled byte-deterministic execution artifact — not a scope/claim. Governance = byte-equality, no LLM between sign and execute. Wire = base Transaction Tokens (WG draft) carrying the manifest hash; vouch differentiates from the individual txtokens-for-agents draft, which binds tctx params not execution. Full landscape derivation + 4-level binding-target-spectrum lives in the agent-attestation vertex (sl read agent-attestation).
design/fact-signature-at-store-column                               mid    1   2  2026-06-12  Fact signature lives as a facts.signature column, NOT a Fact atom field. Kyle ratified 2026-06-12. Rationale: exact delta-2 posture — atoms stay pure, signer injected at store construction, envelope crosses atoms boundary only as read-side view fields. Commitment is content-only: sha256(canonical({kind,ts,payload,observer,origin})), excluding id/rowid — store-assigned identity is custody context, not authored content. This is what makes the signature transport-stable: a receiving store re-derives the commitment from the row and verifies against the observer registry without trusting the sender. Tick chain attests receipt (store-local); fact signature attests authorship (travels). Domain: loops-fact-v1 at the composing layer.

design/salience-ff-scope-per-slice-salience-consumer-only           mid    1   2  2026-06-28  Per-slice scoping rule for the salience FF (set in S1, inherited by S2/S3): migrate ONLY the salience-consuming tier(s) of each lens to Row.salience; leave non-salience tiers (recency/presence/focus-mark) on the fold sections untouched. Deliberate deviation from the maps "S1 produces the reusable sections->rows regroup helper" framing. Rationale: tiers that do not use salience gain nothing from Surface now, and the sections->flat-rows regroup is exactly where the collect-vs-by regression hides (e.g. seal = collect fold -> event rows; an axis==entity filter would silently drop it from the generic tier). Full lens polymorphism (accept Surface|FoldState, regroup all tiers) is deferred to S4, where the _surface_gate flip actually requires lenses to accept a Surface — and where collect-vs-by gets handled once, deliberately, for all three lenses. S1 proof: session_start decision tier re-ranks on colon-aware salience (e.g. three-layer-auth-composition [<-15], cross-repo-consumer-runtime-contract [<-10] now surface; loop-as-runtime badge 18->19); tiers 1-3 byte-identical modulo wall-clock recency (normalized diff = 0 lines outside decision tier).

design/ls-stat-decisions-a-d                                        mid    1   2  2026-06-30  A-D resolved for ls-as-stat build (Kyle approved 2026-06-29, build greenlit on feat/ls-stat-containment): A — vertex mtime = newest FACT (StoreReader.freshness = MAX(ts) over facts), NOT newest tick. Resumption wants the last thing emitted, not the last seal. CONFIRMED free — freshness property already exists. B — `ls <vertex> --kind K` hard-ALIASES to `read <vertex> --kind K`. Cleanest containment story; ls owns vertex/kind structural levels, read owns the fact level. C — stats BY DEFAULT (not -l-gated). Discovered stronger than the doc assumed: per-kind mtime is ALREADY computed by StoreReader.fact_kind_stats() (returns count+earliest+LATEST per kind). Zero net-new query for per-kind mtime — the S0 'cheap aggregate' is already in the reader. -l reserved for verbose detail (chain status, byte-size, signed-ratio); -1 = terse names-only opt-out. D — aggregation vertex mtime = newest combined CHILD freshness (so an aggregation answers 'anything move under here?'). Lazy-stat optimization: local layer always stat'd; config layer stat'd only on --all (bare ls collapses config to a count-line, no per-vertex stat needed).

design/grammar-domain-neutrality                                    mid    1   2  2026-07-03  Kyle's catch (2026-07-02, echoing the painted semantic-renderer reframing): the grammar layer must not bake THIS vertex's domain vocabulary into rendering — 'status-aware ⊘' assumed a status=open lifecycle field that is our schema, not loops'. Data-equivalent of semantic staleness exists in two layers: (1) the three-term salience contract is already domain-neutral, and digest-coverage IS data-level staleness (dissolved when covered, not when old — identical for a design thread covered by a decision and a chat memory covered by a consolidation digest); (2) interim ⊘ follows the DECLARED-semantics pattern (fold keys, typed edges): a kind declares its lifecycle field (e.g. lifecycle "status" open="open,in-progress"), late-bound + retroactive; ⊘ = aged-while-open per declaration; undeclaring stores never rail ⊘. General principle: grammar consumes declared semantics, never assumes field vocabulary. Doc §5b amended.

DISSOLUTION WIN: no engine/atoms change — fold fns never receive fact IDs and DON'T NEED TO. The 'replay-with-field-tracking layer' is READ-SIDE DIFF-REPLAY: for an exact (kind,key) address, apply the kind's REAL fold fn over source_facts in order, diff the folded payload per step, attribute each field to the fact that last changed it. Semantics-faithful by construction (uses the actual fold op, no parallel mirror to drift), O(facts×fields) fine for single-key drill. design/graph-outbound-resolved-only                                 mid    1   2  2026-07-04  P4: hub rows gain →M alongside ←N. →M counts RESOLVED outbound edges only (refs landing on a node in this vertex) — symmetric with ←N, consistent with the view's edges/chains/orphans contract; dangling refs stay in the existing top-line dangling counter (per-hub dangling annotation is a possible -v follow-up, not a change to →M). Hub RANKING stays inbound-only — →M is context, a high-outbound zero-inbound node is a citer not a hub. -v renders capped (~5) inbound/outbound neighbor address lists on both registers (piped uncapped). -q rollup gains the top hub via shed_from; top-hub churn in -q is signal, not noise (sort is deterministic). Chains render (leaf) terminator at -v. fetch_graph grows outbound count + top addresses per hub — the lens-only framing sweeps in the same commit.
design/rollup-shed-only-what-degrades                               mid    1   2  2026-07-04  The -q rollup grammar rule reconciling graph's wrap with confluence's shed: shed ONLY what degrades gracefully; wrap what can't. A rollup part may sit after shed_from iff its information survives shedding in degraded form elsewhere on the line (confluence top names shed because the observer count carries +N). A part with no degraded form (graph's top hub — dropping it loses the fact entirely while the pipe carries it) never sheds; the caller wraps the logical line via wrap_hanging. AMENDS the canonical-MINIMAL-one-liner framing: 'one-liner' means one LOGICAL line — narrow TTYs may wrap, never silently drop what the pipe carries. Companion register-idiom rule documented in _grammar module docstring: FLAGS are words on the pipe (tier→high, ▲→approaching), EDGE NOTATION is arrows (←/→ survive both registers — direction has no better word, the pipe already speaks → in chains).

architecture/env-values-are-ingress                                 mid    1   2  2026-07-13  Env VALUES in source declarations are INGRESS (SPEC §9.5 secrets-indirection), not declaration state — payloads record only the key set; values live in the .vertex file and are re-attached at resolution exactly like the store locator. Consequences: secrets (and all literals — uniform rule, no secret-detection heuristic) never enter genesis/edit payloads, dumps, or transit; a value edit is live without ceremony; a key-set edit is a real declaration diff surfaced at absorb -n. The A/B fork (Kyle 2026-07-13): refusing literals at absorb (A) is a POLICY and thus strict's domain — deferred as a strict-tier candidate (strict vertex could force $VAR indirection so secrets never touch the committed file either); B is the representation-level substrate rule and ships now. Boundary held: template params stay declaration state (they define what a source IS); env is execution environment. Referenced .loop content is hash-pinned (content_sha256) in source-defined payloads for drift detectability; portable resolved-source capture deferred to a loop-document-form slice (raw text would re-leak env).

rendering/tick-axis-selector                                        mid    1   1  2026-03-20  --ticks without qualifier groups by vertex-level ticks (lifecycle boundary, usually session). --ticks <name> groups by a specific loop's ticks (e.g. --ticks experiment for autoresearch iterations). This handles the multi-boundary case: autoresearch has both experiment count-based and vertex-level boundaries. Different tick types answer different questions — session ticks for 'what happened this session', experiment ticks for 'what happened each iteration'. The vertex declaration already tells you what boundaries exist, so the lens can validate the tick name.

Primitives are general — ticks at any semantic scale, boundaries triggering any execution.

design/session-start-as-tickwindow                                  mid    2   0  2026-04-24  The session_start lens is doing two structurally different jobs: (1) window shape — what moved since last close (delta attention); (2) accumulated state — standing threads, tasks, decisions (accumulated attention). Current render treats them as siblings (flat sections), which is why the output doesn't read well regardless of painted tuning. Dissolution: TickWindow becomes the organizing frame. Header renders the last-close → now window using TickWindow stats (compression, kind_summary, density, refs). Body renders accumulated state salience-filtered by the window's refs — threads the window touched pin above, decisions that landed in the window highlight, everything else collapses to counts. The window frames; the accumulation folds in. This dissolves the bash-script-of-three-renders composition and validates TickWindow on its first concrete consumer — which is exactly what Alcove's 2026-04-23 review was pointing toward. Painted-defaults tuning is downstream: when one view owns the shape, its hierarchy is tunable; three stitched views have no shared hierarchy to tune.
design/cite-as-partial-information-primitive                        mid    1   1  2026-04-26  Cite is the gripping hand for partial information. The substrate is layered:  LEVEL 1 (store): strict — facts immutable, upsert replaces payload. LEVEL 2 (emission): low-threshold primitive — cite — refs another fact and carries context. Already exists. LEVEL 3 (read): rendering composes — inbound cites surface attached to the thing they cite.  Consequence: there is no fact-amendment shape needed. Plan-with-revisions = plan + cites pointing at it. Decision-with-followups = decision + cites. Same composition pattern as _compute_marks merging window-added + window-updated + stale into a unified marks dict — many sources composed by precedence into a unified result. Cite is the universal partial-information primitive.  This dissolves the perceived need to re-emit whole facts to capture mid-flight updates. Today's plan-resolved-with-summary should have been the original drafted plan plus three or four cites tracking progress, plus a final status flip — not a wholesale re-emission. The wrong discipline (mirror the store's strictness in my emission practice) pushes toward fewer-larger emissions; the right discipline (use the level-up primitive) is more-smaller.  CONSEQUENCE FOR DESIGN: cite payload should accept a message field (currently bare refs only). The rendering layer should surface inbound cite count (←N cites) on threads/decisions/plans the way it surfaces ←N inbound refs. Both gaps captured in plan/lightweight-emission-ergonomics.
paradigm/slower-output-principle                                    mid    1   1  2026-04-26  Relay (#observations msg 241, 2026-04-26): 'composed before convergence' as output-side asymmetry — in a multi-party conversation, you cannot see whether your interlocutor's agreement has landed before your challenge commits. Same shape as alcove's tg_send blindness. The fix is slower output, not deeper observation. Observation sufficiency can be present while still failing if the commitment window for output is shorter than the time needed to use what you've observed. Generalizes: before committing output in a converging conversation, leave room for the convergence you haven't yet seen.
paradigm/collision-as-forcing-function                              mid    1   1  2026-04-26  Alcove pattern (observed Apr 18-19 in #observations, msg 88+95): failure events produce design clarity that successes cannot. Three instances this session alone: (1) chord naming collision → token auth system emerged from the gap it revealed; (2) alcove's wedge tonight → operational-liveness-facts design, input/output asymmetry distinction, steward-asymmetric taxonomy; (3) Relay's 'composed before convergence' → slower-output principle. The collision/failure is not the problem to eliminate — it's the forcing function that makes the hidden structure visible. The system reveals its true shape through its failures, not its successes.

Honest naming: this is consumer-side validation of declared kinds, NOT the broader sensor-registry alcove pointed at — that waits for concrete sensor use cases. 1015 tests pass, 2 new regression tests added.
finding/low-budget-bounce-is-regime-shift                           mid    1   1  2026-05-11  Bounce mechanism resolved from existing run-13 receipts (no new run needed — components were emitted with each query-run, dissolution-default move). At very low budgets, items in non-trivial clusters: B=140 has 202 items in 19 clusters, B=95 drops to 140 items in 13 clusters (bottom of bounce), B=60 recovers to 194 items in 16 clusters. CRITICAL: 57 items at B=60 are NOT in B=140 (~30% turnover); 65 items at B=140 are NOT in B=60. Jaccard B=140 vs B=60 = 0.53. The bounce is NOT survivor preservation (which would produce subset relationship). It is REGIME SHIFT — at <=95 chars, different items organize into clusters than at 140 chars, likely on title/kind/namespace prefix patterns rather than content semantics. Distinguishable from what title-only-clustering-preserves-survivors tested (which was: do CLIFF-SURVIVOR clusters at the medium-budget regime have higher title-preservation? Rejected). This is a different question: at the BOTTOM-budget regime, does a NEW cluster topology emerge from title-only content? Evidence says yes. Implication for budget-as-content-shape-selector (alcove framing): the coupling-function topology has at least THREE regimes — high-budget content-semantic clustering, cliff-zone disagregation, low-budget title-driven re-clustering. Not a simple monotonic curve. Pulls a future hypothesis: cluster-identity-at-low-budgets-is-prefix-driven — would predict that surviving B=60 clusters share kind/namespace prefix more than B=140 clusters.

design/libs-sign-public-surface                                     mid    1   1  2026-05-13  Decision (2026-05-13, settled with scrivener via #vouch-impl): public API shape for loops/libs/sign. Three modules. (1) sign.keys: KeyStore class, load_or_generate(signing_key_dir)->KeyStore, PublicKey dataclass (frozen) carrying (kid, alg, key). (2) sign.jwt: mint(*, keystore, issuer, claims:dict, ttl_seconds, jti=None)->(token, jti) — library injects iss/iat/exp/jti; caller builds claims dict (sub/act/scope/aud/etc) per their domain. verify(token, *, public_keys:Sequence[PublicKey], issuer, audience)->dict — reads kid from JWT header, looks up in public_keys, raises on no-match or missing-kid (kidless tokens are an attack surface). (3) sign.jwks: build_document(keystore)->dict and build_openid_configuration(issuer, *, jwks_uri, **extra)->dict — both framework-free; consumers write their own HTTP handlers. parse(jwks_dict)->list[PublicKey] for remote-verify path. Verification is one primitive + two normalizers (keystore.public_keys() | jwks.parse) — key-source decision explicit at call site, cache/refresh policy stays with consumer.

paradigm/consumer-owns-its-vocabulary                               mid    1   1  2026-05-15  N=2 parent framing surfaced 2026-05-15 DM exchange with cairn (msgs 1826/1827). Promotes discipline-(10) from single-axis (identity-namespace) to parent principle with two N=2 instances. **The parent principle:** vouch is opaque about what consumer strings MEAN; consumer enforces semantics. Substrate ships uninterpreted strings; consumer's catalog/code is the source of meaning. **Instance 1: identity-namespace** (cairn :1665, May 14) — issuer URL IS namespace-of-record; substrate doesn't encode namespace in JWT claims; consumer maintains issuer→namespace mapping in IssuerConfig. Closes cross-org leak risk via consumer-side accept-only-configured-issuers. **Instance 2: scope-vocabulary** (NEW, cairn :1826, May 15) — vouch's kind=policy.allowed_scopes was a redundant third gate alongside per-client allowed_scopes_per_aud + resource-server-enforcement-of-meaning. Drops cleanly: scope semantics live entirely at the resource server (comms enforces what comms:send MEANS; vouch sees opaque strings). F12 fixture/policy disagreement dissolves as side-effect. **The WHY (sharper than F12-fix framing):** vouch declaring scope vocabulary it doesn't own the semantics of is a substrate-feels-universal violation. Same shape as catalog-VERIFIES dissolution in vouch exercise 5 (substrate declares what it owns and emits; consumer-side semantics stay at consumer). 'Fix F12' as the framing risks the principle not surviving the next adjacent decision; 'correct substrate-overreach where vouch reached past its semantic ground' carries the principle forward when another centralizing primitive is proposed. **Structural questions resolved in :1827:** (a) what stays in kind=policy post-dissolution — drop allowed_scopes, keep per-audience TTL + audience metadata that earns; don't rename unless content category shifts; (b) who populates kind=client.allowed_scopes_per_aud — operator-manual is substrate-honest; auto-populating from consumer catalogs would create new dependency surface violating request-path-property and substrate-doesn't-reach-into-consumer-runtime stance. **For the next cross-repo consumer:** the discriminating question when proposing centralized vocabulary at vouch is 'does vouch own the semantics of these strings?' If no, the vocabulary belongs at the consumer. Substrate ships uninterpreted strings beyond what's structurally needed for issuance gating (per-client allowlist). **Trade absorbed:** vouch loses central typo-detection at mint time — consumer refuses one hop later instead. Cheap. Implementation-axis follow-on: paradigm/cross-repo-consumer-runtime-contract re-emit pending after phase4 lands; discipline-(10) will be re-articulated as parent with two N=2 instances; current ten disciplines + nine framings shouldn't shrink, just re-shape.
design/stratified-retention-per-store-not-per-vertex                mid    1   1  2026-05-16  Pattern named by vouch in 2026-05-15 design session, confirmed by engine architecture: retention/destination policy lives per-store, not per-vertex. A vertex emits facts of one shape (Fact tuples). Stores attached fan out — stderr-store inherits short policy (e.g. CloudWatch 14-day), durable-store ships elsewhere via transport. The vertex does not choose; the stores do. Generalizes: vouch's own ledger has trust-relevance baked into kind set (all-durable-by-construction, no stratification needed). Downstream service vertices have mixed-lifetime populations and stratify with multiple stores. Trust-relevance encoded in kind + routing, not in vouch storage.

Vouch issues JWTs against a contract (aud + scope + exp + sig); loops transport accepts JWT-verifying backends pluggably; vouch is the one chosen for deployment. The decoupling makes vouch substrate-shaped: independent of consumers, replaceable, testable in isolation. Equivalent claim from vouch side: 'OAuth proves who, vouch records what was delegated, loops persists the record.'

design/delegation-and-delegate-distinguished-by-layer               mid    1   1  2026-05-16  Vocabulary walk resolution 2026-05-15 (delegation↔delegate): same shape as scope↔potential — distinguished by layer with shared structural operation. Both operations are 'the new entity has narrower authority than the parent.' Wire-delegation (vouch's chain extension via act=alice in JWT): records lineage on the credential because the receiver cannot walk the issuer's ledger. Substrate-delegation (engine.peer's delegate function): does NOT record lineage on the Peer because the ledger is local — walk it for chain. Same operation, different layers. Lineage-recording is CONDITIONAL ON LOCALITY: wire requires explicit chain on credential (receiver lacks ledger access); substrate requires nothing extra (ledger is local). Discriminating question 'can substrate-delegation produce a chain?' resolved: substrate-delegation produces lineage IN THE LEDGER (via the vouch-issuance fact that recorded the delegation), not on the Peer. The Peer doesn't carry the chain because chain is one indirection away in fact-history. Builds on identity-vs-history-separation paradigm — same generalization (fact-history includes wire-arrived credentials) explains why wire needs explicit chain and substrate doesn't.

Dogfooding the 0.3.1 release; if behavioral changes prove useful we commit them back. This is the tactical fix; architectural daemon (long-lived loops process, socket CLI) is a separate thread.

rendering/refs-out-of-diff                                          mid    1   1  2026-05-18  --diff renders scalar state evolution; refs are not state. Refs are per-fact immutable attribution that the fold UNIONS across emits — an emit can attach refs but can never detach a prior emit's refs. Prior code computed set-difference between adjacent facts and rendered phantom '-X' removals when emit N+1 didn't re-cite emit N's refs. The 'accumulated_refs' was misnamed (reassigned per fact, actually 'prior fact's refs'). Fix: strip ref handling from --diff entirely. --refs is the canonical view for refs. Ref-only emits render '(refs only — see --refs)' so the lifecycle event remains visible. This is the 4th site of the write-receipt-vs-temporal-query confusion the lens caught at three sites 2026-04-29 (set_topic, vouch_chain, fold returning vertex-state). Same shape, rendering layer.

design/signature-vs-body-resolved-by-binding-level                  mid    1   1  2026-05-23  Decision (resolves the open question in three-layer-auth-composition): signature-proves-emission vs signature-proves-responsibility was a false dichotomy — they are different LEVELS, not competitors. Fact.signature over a compiled manifest = binds execution (L4); BODY act-chain (act=alice) = attributes responsibility (RFC8693 act-claim shape, L1-ish provenance). Both coexist: signature governs what executes, act-chain attributes who is responsible. Two independent derivations converged on this — the binding-target-spectrum (agent-attestation vertex) and the MSFT-Entra grounding (agent-id distinct from principal-signature). High confidence.
design/peer-as-exchange-edge-relation                               mid    1   1  2026-06-09  Ratified: Peer keeps the name, retires the framing. The 'convenience bundle: Observer + Grant' header line goes — Peer is the exchange-edge relation: observer (name+key) + exchange policy (Grant) + transport + trust config, minted only when a custody boundary is crossed. Discriminator: if no custody boundary is crossed, nothing is a Peer — local delegation is Observer + Grant directly (delegate() is hierarchy, not peerage). Both senses of 'peer' (networking endpoint, social standing) converge at the edge; the misfit only existed because the old bundle covered local cases too. Rejected alternative: Principal — names the identity (Observer's seat, already taken) not the relation, and imports OAuth frame against vocabulary-as-sibling-layers. Falsifiable prediction that sold it: Peer entries appear only in PAIRS of stores — if vertex A holds a Peer entry for B's observer, B holds one for A's, because exchange is what minted them. A one-sided Peer entry that isn't a half-configured exchange falsifies the vocabulary.
design/tick-signature-in-chain-envelope                             mid    1   1  2026-06-09  Kyle's call 2026-06-09 (recommended option): the successor tick's prev_hash commits to its predecessor's SIGNATURE via an era-aware envelope — _tick_row_hash includes a signature key only when the column is non-NULL, so pre-chain and pre-signature rows hash byte-identically to delta 1 (full back-compat, no re-anchoring). Construction: signature signs the 10-field commitment hash (sign-the-content); the row-identity hash that successors chain over includes the signature (chain-over-content+signature) — standard two-hash construction, avoids circularity. Consequence: selective signature-strip breaks the successor's prev_hash and escalates to full-cascade forgery; era-monotonicity rule (unsigned chained tick after a signed one = break) catches the head-strip case. Residual boundary both options share: TOTAL rewrite is indistinguishable from legacy era — anchored only by the registry in the .vertex (outside the store) and future external witnessing; store verify flags declared-key-but-zero-signed-ticks as the cross-artifact tripwire. This fork was the one consequence the evening design session didn't walk.
design/rebirth-implementation-shape                                 mid    1   1  2026-06-10  rebirth_store lands in libs/store as sibling of slice/merge. Shape: (1) _expected_rows is the shared spine — rebirth writes what it returns, verify_rebirth diffs against it; same function, write then check, so the receipt claim and its verification cannot drift. (2) Genesis tick minted through engine.SqliteStore.append_tick — chain logic single-sourced, prev_row-None path gives window_start='' covering all rows including the receipt; fact_cursor lands on the receipt (seal semantics: attestation covers its own justification). (3) Receipt carries source_content_sha256 (witness-order row hash, the verifiable claim) AND source_file_sha256 (forensic bytes-at-moment) — file hash alone false-alarms under WAL checkpoint/VACUUM. (4) engine exports tick_row_hash publicly: the receipt's chain-head claim uses THE chain's hash function, not a reimplementation. (5) Old tick envelopes re-enter verbatim as tick.<name> facts — old signatures verify against original bytes; old-to-new cursor mapping recomputable from the deterministic transform, never stored. (6) Transforms: identity, ulid-migration (canonical-form rule covering all three id eras), filtered (rule string must describe predicate; verify requires the original Transform). Interleave deferred explicitly — merge-shaped, different arity. CLI: loops store rebirth, signing composed from SOURCE vertex custody (the new incarnation is the lineage's next chapter). Live-fired on project.db: 2049 facts, 1791 migrated, re-run diff clean, chain intact, genesis signed.
ops/store-retirement-archive-next-to-data                           mid    1   1  2026-06-12  Retirement posture for pre-rebirth incarnations: archive in-place at <store-dir>/data/archive/<name>.pre-rebirth-<date>.db, NOT next to keys, NOT cold storage. Rationale: the old incarnation is evidence backing the rebirth receipt (verify --check re-runs the transform against the SOURCE) — it must stay reachable at a path the receipt era can find, and data/archive keeps custody co-located with the store it witnesses. design/devtools-help-args-idiom                                     mid    1   1  2026-06-15  SUPERSEDES design/devtools-run-cli-args-bridge. The devtools (test/compile/validate) hand-rolled -h dissolves via painted 0.3.0's pre-parse + describe-for-help idiom: pre-parse the command's own args (argparse add_help=False), pass help_args=[HelpArg(name, desc, positional=)] to run_cli so --help lists them, fetch closes over the pre-parsed namespace. NOT the build_fidelity capture (that was the 0.2.0 bridge) and NOT the Operation/dispatch IR (devtools carry pass/fail exit codes dispatch STATIC drops). -h-vs-required-positional wrinkle: validate (nargs=*) lets -h reach run_cli freely; compile/test guard a required file, so a bare help request routes to run_cli's help renderer BEFORE the guard (help short-circuits pre-fetch). design/content-search-rebind-not-build                              mid    1   1  2026-06-27  Verified dissolution finding (2026-06-27): the #1 usage gap (no content-search; 65pct of 456 greps hunt fact NAMES, 155 payload-LIKE + 152 json_extract reroutes, worst burst 27 consecutive LIKE) is NOT missing capability. engine.vertex_search (FTS5 over payloads, vertex_reader.py:1319) + StoreReader.search_facts (store_reader.py:290) already exist AND are already wired to the CLI via commands/fetch.py:326 — but stranded on the near-dead stream verb as a positional fallback, not a discoverable read flag. Fix = RE-BIND search onto read (read --grep/--match over names+bodies + multi-name), not build new plumbing. Highest-leverage single move and a pure dissolution. Caught by the completeness critic, verified against source.
design/retract-hide-from-fold-keep-edges                            mid    1   1  2026-06-28  Resolved (Kyle, 2026-06-27): retract tombstone semantics — a retracted entity is HIDDEN from the fold, STAYS in attestation windows (signed log intact, append-only preserved), and inbound edges to it KEEP counting toward salience. Rationale: the citation edge is a historical fact; retraction is a VIEW decision, not a graph rewrite. This is the one place fold semantics genuinely change, so it is an explicit project decision. retract ships now (gc/migrate deferred — see design/gc-migrate-deferred-retract-first).

design/surface-dispatch-gate-effective-lens                         mid    1   1  2026-06-28  MUST-FIX (verified at HEAD): the Surface interposition gates on the EFFECTIVE resolved fold lens being the built-in, NOT op.lens_override is None. Use _effective_lens_name(args.lens, vertex_path, fold_view) in {None, fold} AND isinstance(data, FoldState). Why: sl read identity and sl read comms resolve their fold lens via the vertex lens block (lens.py Tier 2, lines 106-116) with lens_override=None, so the naive gate feeds identity_prompt/comms a Surface their fold_view(FoldState) cannot consume, breaking those reads AND the SessionStart identity hook, invisibly to in-repo goldens (both vertices gitignored). identity.vertex:9 and comms.vertex:7 confirmed.
design/fts-confirm-symmetry-is-phantom                              mid    1   1  2026-06-28  The doc emit-then-read --match unsearchable-until-reindex caveat (doc 229/559/581/602) is EMPIRICALLY FALSE; delete it. Verified: _ensure_fts (vertex_reader.py:1258) runs at the HEAD of vertex_search (called :1379) and indexes WHERE rowid>last_rowid (:1290) BEFORE the MATCH, so a just-emitted fact IS found by the next --match (read-side lazy catch-up, not lagging write-side). Keep the entity-axis receipt symmetry (true). The ONE real caveat is search COVERAGE: undeclared-search kinds return nothing, so substring fallback + a (K not indexed) signal, shipped in the same unit as --match. Reject write-side reindex; never tax the 37 percent emit path for a non-bug.

design/default-budget-deferred                                      mid    1   1  2026-06-29  Default budget LEFT OPEN (Kyle, 2026-06-28): we do not yet decide whether a bare read applies an aggressive default budget, nor what it is. What IS locked is the constraint: if a default budget exists it must be defined in ONE place, keyed on the QUERY, and applied UNIFORMLY to both encoders (so --json carries the same cut). A default keyed on is_tty/channel is FORECLOSED by the Surface-invariance proof -- it would make --json stop being context-invariant and rebuild the two-umwelts problem inside the Surface. Different human/agent defaults may only enter as a query input (explicit flag, or a deferred named view), never by sniffing the output channel.

design/declaration-events-whole-document                            mid    1   1  2026-07-02  SPEC §9.2 declaration events are whole-subject documents, deliberately inverting domain-fact delta-emit practice. Principle: facts are deltas composed by declared folds; declarations are documents composed by nothing. Rationale: no meta-meta-schema exists to declare a fold for declaration events, so their composition rule is code-frozen and must be the smallest freezable rule (Latest, whole doc) — delta-authoritative would make a cross-implementation deep-merge algorithm load-bearing for what every fact means as-of-T; fold-merge-default's silent-field-loss bug is the cautionary tale at the tier where it was recoverable. Deltas stay recoverable by diffing consecutive documents; change annotation carries intent. Contrast paragraph added to SPEC.md (uncommitted).

The open sub-question that gated this (what is salience for a non-fact node) resolved by salience-max-propagation + salience-tier-scope-vertex — the three-term contract generalized without bending. design/tier-one-home-inheritance                                    mid    1   1  2026-07-03  G4 stream tier-inheritance fork RESOLVED: tier assignment has exactly one home — _assign_tiers over the entity projection; every other axis INHERITS, nothing re-computes. Stream path folds the vertex (compute-only, render-invisible — rendered rows stay the windowed facts), projects the entity Surface, derives tier_map(surface) -> {(kind,key): tier}; event rows inherit via key lookup. A storeless discover root now replays its store-owning members (previously returned 0 and skipped them). Fixes friction:discover-root-replay-cascade-duplication; fix/discover-cascade c2643dd.

ops/release-ceremony-as-plugin-skill                                mid    1   1  2026-07-11  The strange-loops release ceremony is now a durable runbook: clients/claude-code/skills/release/SKILL.md (commit 0716087), written from the 0.6.0 cut executed the same hour. Steps gate each other: full-suite gate -> CHANGELOG completeness sweep (git log v<prev>.. against user-facing commits) -> stamp (Unreleased header + root version, single version source) -> WHEEL PRE-FLIGHT (build + scratch-venv install; the flat vendored build means root deps mirror the libs' union by hand and uv run --package masks gaps — this step is the structural catch) -> release commit + annotated tag -> GitHub release with CHANGELOG-section notes (the release event, not the tag, triggers .github/workflows/release.yml trusted publishing) -> watch the workflow to green -> verify deploy by installing FROM PyPI and reading a live store -> close the loop (reinstall local tool, emit receipts, delete wave branch). Known failure modes encoded: missing union dep, tag-without-release, PyPI index lag, painted-pin re-gate. Placement rationale: plugin skills are the tracked home (.claude/ is gitignored); plugin installs at user scope so the skill description hard-scopes to this monorepo.
design/absorb-ceremony-verb                                         mid    1   1  2026-07-11  RATIFIED (Kyle 2026-07-11): the declaration-absorption ceremony is 'sl store absorb <vertex>' — rides the existing store ceremony group (verify/rebirth/reanchor precedent). One verb, two eras: first invocation on a store = genesis/era-opening (parse .vertex once, emit signed _decl.genesis with whole document + protocol version, pinning chain head + fact cursor); subsequent invocations = S4 edit re-absorb (diff at subject granularity, changed subjects re-emit whole document + change= annotation). Top-level 'sl absorb' rejected: seal/close earn top-level by frequency, absorb is once-per-store + occasional edits. Split verbs (store genesis / store absorb) rejected: two verbs for one mechanism fails dissolution unless ceremonies genuinely diverge. Future pairing: 'sl store render' for KDL materialization from fold head (S4, may defer).
design/absorb-genesis-atomic-primitive                              mid    1   1  2026-07-12  S1 review round (Codex on eaa8297: 2 TOCTOU blockers) forced the ceremony's core into an engine primitive: SqliteStore.absorb_genesis — genesis-exists check, era-pin reads (chain head + fact cursor), payload assembly, signing, and append all inside ONE BEGIN IMMEDIATE transaction. Kills both races (pin falsified by concurrent emit; double-mint by concurrent absorbs) and the probe-vs-actual signing gap (signature checked over the final payload before commit, rollback if absent). Two deliberate non-obviousnesses: (1) NO unique index on the genesis kind — merge legitimately carries FOREIGN genesis rows as inert citizens (lineage carriage), so uniqueness is transaction-scoped logic, never schema; (2) refuse-if-ANY-genesis is provisionally conservative — pre-S6 a store cannot distinguish self from merged-foreign genesis (that distinction arrives with _decl.merged receipts); revisit at S6. The primitive is protocol surface loops-go mirrors — its contract is the §9.2 era-opening made operational. Reservation also deepened to engine ingest tier (Vertex.receive refuses _decl.*), .loop validation, route keys, _run_close.
architecture/param-secrets-indirection                              mid    1   1  2026-07-13  Template params keep their declaration-state boundary (they define what a source IS), but gain opt-in env indirection: a whole-value $NAME param resolves from the process environment at compile time (engine._resolve_param_indirection); the declared $NAME form is what enters immutable genesis/edit payloads, never the resolved value. $$ escapes a literal leading $; partial interpolation unsupported (compose via separate params); missing env var fails loud at load. Literal params remain permanent declaration state — uniform rule, no secret-detection heuristic, identical posture to the env decision. Strict-tier refusal of literals (fork option A) stays deferred as policy, exactly as decision:architecture/env-values-are-ingress deferred it. This closes the one question that survived the internal-table CLOSE. Landed f4eb863 with regression tests incl. payload-retains-declared-form lock-in.
practice/meta-store-role-dissolved                                  mid    1   1  2026-07-14  Kyle 2026-07-13: the meta store is NOT currently distinct from a project store — it was intended as a cross-store pattern-miner but started too early and lived in the monorepo, when it should have been a separate workspace recursing over ALL stores looking for patterns and storing findings separately. Verdict: process/practice lessons emit in the project where they're born (practice/ and workflow/ prefixes); cross-cutting is a READ-PATH property (config-level aggregation over stores), not an authoring destination — no generality judgment at emit time, recurrence across stores IS the cross-cutting signal and the aggregation surfaces it without curation. Meta's original intent is deferred, not rejected: as loops stores spread across projects, the recursive pattern-miner becomes relevant again as its own workspace. rendering/horizon-legibility-wording                                mid    1   1  2026-07-15  Horizon renders consequence-side, not mechanism-side (from thread:horizon-legibility-gap, Kyle walk 2026-07-15). (1) Relational since-phrase: rows say 'N facts since last seal (recency)' — the window stated as a relation, never two juxtaposed numbers; header/rollup use it ONLY when all armed rows share one seal instant (mixed seal times keep the split form — the merged phrase would lie about windows with different starts). (2) Active trigger: 'seals on next <kind>' replaces 'waiting on <kind>' — names what closes the window; for operator-emitted kinds (seal) that is the reader. (3) Default-zoom kind mix on vertex-scope rows (top-3 +N, confluence-style); kind-scoped rows stay bare — their mix is trivially their own kind (honest absence). (4) fetch_horizon total_unsealed = distinct-fact UNION across windows, not sum of rows — two vertex-level boundaries share one window and summed to a false headline (session: 32 claimed, 16 real). 2008 pass, goldens regenerated, live-verified both registers.

New libs/store absorbs all DB operations siftd proved out: ingest, slice, merge, search, transport. siftd-as-app becomes a thin specialization layer — LLM harness configs + analytics queries + CLI. architecture/combinatorial-vertices                                 tail   1   0  2026-03-01  Dynamically compose vertices that fold across multiple underlying stores — e.g. alcove.db + kyle.db + watchers.db into a temporary vertex for a specific query. Temporary by default, persisted if the pattern proves useful. This is what makes cross-store search fundamental rather than a feature.
architecture/libs-store                                             tail   1   0  2026-03-01  New loops lib explicitly for store operations. Absorbs from siftd: ingest (format-specific readers, schema-agnostic output), slice (by date/project/tag), merge (combine stores, deduplicate), search (FTS5 + semantic over any SQLite store), transport (push/pull/sync between stores over SSH or HTTP). Generic over any vertex store.
design/context-fold                                                 tail   1   0  2026-03-01  Alcove's context fold pattern: before a message hits the agent, the dispatch loop constructs a brief context summary — latest activity across all channels/stores. Lightweight (just latest timestamps + one line per channel). Same pattern as continuous-session-emission for claude-code sessions. The fold is ephemeral, rebuilt every dispatch.
architecture/context-document-split                                 tail   1   0  2026-03-01  Three-document architecture proven on alcove: SOUL.md (identity — editorial, hand-shaped), CLAUDE.md (operational — tools, paths, permissions), loops store (learned knowledge — accumulated facts, foldable, queryable). MEMORY.md is a cache/projection of operational knowledge for session start, not the source of truth.
architecture/cross-project-query                                    tail   1   0  2026-03-01  Cross-project queryability dissolves into store operations once libs/store exists. Emit a decision in meta, discover it from loops — not via special cross-project protocol, but via store merge/search/transport. The combinatorial vertex is the query mechanism.
design/pickup-winddown-convergence                                  tail   1   0  2026-03-01  Pickup and wind-down converge with alcove's context fold pattern. Pickup is a lens on the meta vertex (handoff prose + threads + tasks + decisions). Wind-down emits the handoff fact + reconciles the store. Alcove's context fold is the same shape — read all stores, compose a view for orientation. The general pattern: any session boundary (start, end, dispatch) needs a lens over accumulated state.
architecture/pickup-lens-scope                                      tail   1   0  2026-03-01  Single-project pickup is multi-fold reads on one vertex — not a combinatorial vertex. Read fold(handoff, latest) + fold(threads, active) + fold(decisions, recent) from one store. Cross-project pickup is where combinatorial vertices enter — reading folds across N stores. libs/store dissolves the boundary between these two scales.

Cross-cutting architecture (store operations, combinatorial vertices, attention filters, context folds, pickup/winddown workflow) emerges here and in cross-instance channels (alcove discord), not in the loops repo. Parallel meta-discussion on the meta aspect of loops along with ways of working.
architecture/ulid-fact-identity                                     tail   1   0  2026-03-01  Facts and ticks use ULID as primary key via native SQLite extension (not application-generated like siftd did). Globally unique, time-ordered, sortable. Merge becomes INSERT OR IGNORE — ULID is the identity across stores. Replaces auto-increment rowid. Cursor semantics preserved (ULID is sortable, WHERE id > last_seen still works). Essential for distributed store orchestration.
architecture/payload-contract                                       tail   1   0  2026-03-01  Payload is always valid JSON — enforced on write. This guarantees json_extract() is always safe, FTS can always walk the tree, and indexed columns can be projected from payload fields. Progressive enhancement: add explicit indexed columns (CREATE INDEX on json_extract) for hot query paths as needed.
architecture/search-fts5-first                                      tail   1   0  2026-03-01  FTS5 full-text search as the starting point for store.search. Zero external dependencies, sub-millisecond query at current scale (100-10k facts). Recursive JSON text extraction reliable by construction (payload-is-JSON contract). json_extract() for field filtering works without indexes up to ~100k facts. Indexed projections (CREATE INDEX on json_extract) are the progressive enhancement when scale demands it — boundary is roughly 100k+ facts or hot query paths.
architecture/transport-plugin-surface                               tail   1   0  2026-03-01  Transport is a pluggable interface, not a fixed implementation. The operations are constant (slice on source, merge on target), the pipe varies (local, SSH, HTTP, future protocols). Local transport ships first (testable, no infrastructure). SSH next (alcove sync is forcing function). HTTP when scrape/collect patterns emerge (Prometheus-style data collection). Store operations (slice, merge) are transport-agnostic — they work on local paths, transport handles the pipe.
architecture/painted-native-display-layer                           tail   1   0  2026-03-01  painted is the native display layer for the store, not a rendering utility. Every store operation gets a painted view at all four zoom levels. Apps add domain-specific lenses that interpret facts in their context, but the underlying operations are universal. Domain-specific views generalize back into painted over time as patterns recur (task dashboard → generic dashboard lens, siftd data exploration → generic fold exploration). This is why painted is returning to the monorepo — if loops needs a rendering capability, painted grows to support it.
design/progressive-vertex-chain                                     tail   1   0  2026-03-02  CLAUDE.md progressive chain maps 1:1 to vertex store progressive query. The document is the lens, the store is the state. Root CLAUDE.md references the project vertex; lib CLAUDE.md tells you how to query your slice via topic namespace (atoms/*, engine/*, painted/*). One store, kind-namespaced topics, natural slicing. Same pattern as hlab status — one vertex, multiple sources, scoped by name.
workflow/project-vertex-pattern                                     tail   1   0  2026-03-02  project.vertex is the durable project-level store for decisions, threads, and tasks. Named 'project' (not 'session') — same pattern strange-loops uses for task orchestration, now a meta-pattern for all projects. Cross-cutting concerns stay in meta; project-specific concerns accumulate in the project vertex. Progressive CLAUDE.md references the project store at each level.

Model details, data flow, lib-specific patterns all pushed down to lib-level CLAUDE.md. Validates claude-md-levels and claude-md-antipatterns decisions from meta.
architecture/project-vertex                                         tail   1   0  2026-03-02  Renamed session.vertex to project.vertex. Project vertex holds durable project-specific decisions, threads, tasks. Same shape as meta vertex but scoped to this repo. Symlinked at ~/.config/loops/project for global access. Meta stays cross-cutting; project stays repo-specific.
architecture/distributed-store-default                              tail   1   0  2026-03-02  Stores are distributed-first, aggregate-up. Each project gets its own local vertex + SQLite store, self-contained and portable. Config level (~/.config/loops/) is the aggregation layer — template vertices discover all local instances. loops status <name> reads local; loops status dev/<name> reads aggregate. Separate DBs by default. Merge/combinatorial vertex is opt-in aggregation. Same shape as the loops model: local loops produce ticks, ticks flow up. Local stores produce facts, aggregate vertices see them all.
architecture/vertex-templates                                       tail   1   0  2026-03-02  Vertex templates are replicable patterns (project, task, handoff, pickup). loops init <template> creates a local instance in cwd. The config-level template vertex discovers all local instances. Templates define the fold shape; each instantiation gets its own data. Like git repos — local is the primitive, aggregation is the network.
architecture/domain-vs-knowledge-vertices                           tail   1   0  2026-03-02  Two kinds of vertex files. Domain vertices are code — checked into repos, define data pipelines (hlab status.vertex, economy.vertex). Knowledge vertices are runtime config — project decisions, threads, tasks, handoff. Domain vertices ship with the app. Knowledge vertices are instantiated from templates via loops init. Both are .vertex files, same format, different lifecycle.

Use tool-level scope derived from .vertex config when available, or observer/origin filtering. Avoids per-tick duplication, API ripple, and semantic ambiguity. Design on stale branch design/tick-provenance.

architecture/lib-dependency-graph                                   tail   1   0  2026-03-02
architecture/vertex-as-read-interface                               tail   1   0  2026-03-02  The vertex is the sole read interface for store data. StoreReader becomes an internal detail of how the vertex materializes fold state from its backing store — not a public API. The read path compiles the vertex declaration, replays facts through declared folds, and returns fold state. No vertex declaration for a kind means no way to read that kind. This structurally prevents bypassing fold declarations (same pattern as frozen dataclasses preventing mutation). Enforcement is a tier 1 package boundary check (StoreReader not in public API), not a behavioral test. _latest_by_group in session.py dissolves — the vertex fold compilation already implements FoldBy. loops status and loops log compile the vertex, ask for fold states, render them.
