architecture/dissolved-apps                                         tail   1   0  2026-03-02
architecture/progressive-claude-apps-complete                       tail   1   0  2026-03-02
architecture/app-dispatch-pattern                                   tail   1   0  2026-03-02  Apps register a short name in an explicit dict in loops/main.py. loops <app> <args> delegates to the app's main(argv) via importlib. ~5 lines. Phase 1 is a static registry; entry-point discovery deferred until 3+ apps stabilize. The app owns its own command dispatch, fetch functions, and lenses. The boundary is main(argv) — loops CLI doesn't know about app internals, app doesn't know about loops CLI dispatch.
design/lens-generalization-flow                                     tail   1   0  2026-03-02  Domain-specific lenses generalize to painted when the same rendering pattern appears in 2+ apps. This happens naturally — don't extract ahead of time. Generic store lenses (fact timeline, fold state views) live in painted. Domain lenses (siftd search results, task lifecycle) stay in the app. The signal to extract is independent convergence, not prediction.
architecture/rendering-three-layers                                 tail   1   0  2026-03-02  Three-layer rendering architecture: (1) painted owns structural primitives (Block, Line, zoom, run_cli), timestamp formatting, and generic data patterns like record timelines — parameterized, domain-agnostic. (2) apps/loops owns store atom rendering (fact_line, tick_line, log_block) that maps facts/ticks to painted's structural patterns, plus the default payload lens (content_gist heuristic). (3) Domain apps provide per-kind payload lenses that override the default. painted never imports from atoms/engine.
design/payload-lens                                                 tail   1   0  2026-03-02  A payload lens is a single function (kind, payload, zoom) → str | Block. At zoom 0 it returns a one-liner gist. At zoom 2+ it returns a multi-line expansion. content_gist and _log_summary dissolve into this — they were always the same concept at different zoom levels. The structural renderer (fact_line, log_block) composes with the payload lens via a summarize callback. Apps inject domain-specific payload lenses; the default is heuristic field scanning.
architecture/painted-record-patterns                                tail   1   0  2026-03-02  painted grows generic record rendering patterns: timestamped record lines, date-grouped timelines, fold-state tables. These are parameterized by a payload lens — painted handles the chrome (timestamps, grouping, zoom degradation, width), the caller provides meaning. Facts, ticks, blog entries, log lines — all are timestamped records with fields. The structural shape is the same; the payload lens provides the domain interpretation.
architecture/store-search-layer                                     tail   1   0  2026-03-02  FTS5 is required infrastructure, not optional. Spec-declared searchable fields in vertex KDL (search "field1" "field2" as sibling of fold/boundary). Standalone FTS5 table with lazy catch-up indexing via high water mark — no INSERT triggers because spec-to-field mapping lives in vertex, not database. Write path untouched; FTS is purely read-side. First search pays backfill cost, subsequent searches catch up on deltas. Combinatorial vertex search: each store searched independently, results merged after recall. json_extract+LIKE rejected — personal scale grows continuously (siftd alone 100-150k+ facts), cross-store combinatorial queries multiply dataset.
architecture/boundary-enforcement                                   tail   1   0  2026-03-02  AST-based architecture boundary tests in tests/test_architecture.py enforce vertex-as-read-interface. Four rules: apps don't import StoreReader (exceptions: store inspector permanent, pop_store temporary), apps don't import sqlite3, libs don't import apps, lib dependency DAG (engine->lang runtime, engine->atoms runtime). TYPE_CHECKING-aware visitor. Stale exceptions fail the test. Monorepo-level concern, lives at repo root not in any single lib.
architecture/vertex-search-declaration                              tail   1   0  2026-03-02  Vertex spec declares searchable fields per kind: search "field1" "field2" as sibling of fold and boundary in loop definitions. LoopDef gains search: tuple[str, ...]. Callers don't override at query time — vertex_search reads the spec to know what's searchable. Only declared fields extracted and indexed. Keeps FTS5 index surgical at scale. Template loop resolution via collect_search_fields() handles generated kind names from .loop templates.
design/lazy-fts-indexing                                            tail   1   0  2026-03-02  FTS5 indexing uses lazy catch-up pattern: first search pays full backfill, subsequent searches catch up on deltas via high water mark in fts_state table. No INSERT triggers — triggers can't do spec-aware field extraction since the kind-to-field mapping lives in the vertex file, not the database. The resultant first-search slowdown fits the loops philosophy: not necessary that things happen instantly, only that they do reliably with the same data flow and rule set. Idempotent, incremental, spec-driven.
design/combinatorial-vertex-search                                  tail   1   0  2026-03-02  Cross-store search follows recall-then-compose pattern: FTS5 per store independently, union candidate sets, fold/rank across combined results. Composition happens after recall, not during — FTS5 virtual tables are per-database in SQLite. Each vertex store remains self-contained with its own FTS5 index. Combinatorial vertex is a view over stores, not a new store. Search follows the same boundary.
design/app-dissolution                                              tail   1   0  2026-03-02  Apps dissolve into lenses + feedback over vertex declarations. An app does not own a data model or ingress pipeline — the vertex declaration (kinds, folds, search fields, boundaries) IS the data model, Sources ARE ingress, and both ship via template at loops init. What an app uniquely provides: (1) domain-specific lenses — Painted rendering of fold state tuned to a data shape (conversation browser, task board, system dashboard), and (2) feedback capability — the ability to emit facts/ticks back through the lens (tag a conversation, close a task, ack an alert). The observer and actor are the same entity. This dissolves siftd, strange-loops, and hlab into structurally identical programs: Painted surfaces over vertex state with domain-specific rendering and keybindings. The Smalltalk parallel is precise — there is one runtime (loops), one data substrate (vertex/store), one rendering framework (Painted), and domain configuration that selects active lenses and feedback handlers. The app is a perspective on the system, not a separate program. Unlike Smalltalk, the Unix grounding holds: stores are cp-able SQLite files, sources are shell commands, CLI is always available as pipe-friendly lower-fidelity surface.
design/store-ingest-dissolution                                     tail   1   0  2026-03-02  The store-ingest-design plan dissolves. Ingest — format-aware file reading that produces facts — is not a library primitive. It decomposes into: Sources (shell commands or scripts that read files and emit NDJSON, already exist), parse pipeline (dict→dict shaping vocabulary, already exists), and vertex declaration (kind/fold configuration, already exists). siftd's adapters are Sources that haven't been written as Sources yet — each adapter's discover→parse pipeline is equivalent to a script that reads conversation files and emits structured records. The three-tier loading (built-in < entry point < drop-in) becomes: template ships default source scripts, user overrides with project-local scripts. The read_file/ingest_to_store API proposed for libs/store is unnecessary — format-aware file reading is a script concern, not a library primitive. Bulk historical import is an edge case solved by a script, not a library. What remains from the store-operations-design plan (receive, compact, transport) is genuine new infrastructure — moving stores between locations does not dissolve into existing primitives.
design/actions-on-the-loop                                          tail   1   0  2026-03-02  Actions with side effects (task send spawns a worktree, task merge runs git operations) are not special-cased command handlers — they are facts on the loop. Emitting task.dispatch places the intent on the wire; something observes it and executes the side effect; the outcome emits as a further fact; the boundary folds the cascade. The CLI command and TUI keypress are different input surfaces for the same emission. This is not the mature future form — it is the design. If we build it this way from the start, the system composes: any observer can react to any fact, boundaries track lifecycle across the full cascade, and the audit trail is complete. Custom domain logic that does not dissolve — worktree management, subprocess spawning, git operations — lives in the observer/tick handler that reacts to the intent fact, not in the CLI command that emits it.
architecture/app-registration                                       tail   1   0  2026-03-02  Apps register three things: lenses (read fold state → render at fidelity levels), feedback handlers (user input → emit fact/tick), and action observers (react to intent facts with side effects). The harness makes all three available as both CLI commands and TUI keybindings at appropriate fidelity. There is no separate app scaffold per domain — the directory structure, CLI dispatch, dev harness are identical. What differentiates siftd from strange-loops from hlab is: which vertex declaration (template), which lenses (Painted components), which feedback/action handlers (domain logic). The registration mechanism is the app's interface to the system.
design/lens-modifiers                                               tail   1   0  2026-03-02  Lens rendering composes through modifiers, not separate lens implementations. Four modifier types identified from the painted-log-line-demo research: (1) Gutter — colored left edge encoding one dimension (lifecycle stage, health, freshness). Follows Grafana/Datadog pattern, underused in terminals. (2) Attention — dim low-information-gain records, highlight high. First-occurrence errors are high attention, 47th occurrence is noise. Decisions on new topics are high, routine ticks are low. This connects to the attention-filter design. (3) History arc — show evolution over time (thread exploring→active→decided, experiment proposed→graduated). Records are trajectories, not points. (4) Density — vertical space per record, controlled by Zoom enum. These compose freely: task board = record_timeline + gutter(lifecycle) + attention(staleness). Thread pipeline = record_timeline + history_arc + attention(readiness). Channel response = attention(high_only) + density(MINIMAL).
design/rendering-semantics                                          tail   1   0  2026-03-02  Six design principles from log line research ground the rendering vocabulary. (1) Color encodes exactly one dimension — severity OR source, never both. (2) INFO is baseline, color marks deviation — journalctl principle. (3) Fixed-width metadata columns + variable message = scannable — Docker Compose pattern. (4) Severity gutter is underused in terminals — Grafana/Datadog colored left edge, minimal footprint, instantly scannable. (5) Continuation indentation beats prefix repetition for multi-line — lnav principle. (6) Width-aware rendering is a gap in terminal tools — an opportunity for Painted to own. Additionally: the PayloadLens pattern (kind, payload, zoom) → str|Block is the domain extension point. Default rendering handles unknown kinds via well-known key extraction. Domain lenses (loops_lens, siftd_lens) override with kind-specific formatting. Lenses compose with modifiers — the lens provides content, the modifier provides visual treatment.
design/composition-primitives                                       tail   1   0  2026-03-02  Three composition primitives for rendering vertex data, each matching a different data shape. (1) record_timeline — groups by date, temporal data. Natural for session logs, task activity, change history. Already built in painted-log-line-demo. (2) record_map — groups by key hierarchy (namespace tree), topological data. Natural for decision landscapes (testing/*, architecture/*), tag views, observer groupings. Zoom: MINIMAL = group names + counts, SUMMARY = group + latest record, DETAILED = all records within groups. Being designed now. (3) record_line — the atomic unit. Single timestamped record at a zoom level. All composition primitives delegate to record_line for individual records. PayloadLens and modifiers apply at record_line level and propagate through any composition primitive. A fourth primitive — spatial/graph/canvas — is under research for relationship data (fact dependency chains, store topology, cross-project impact).
design/canvas-primitive                                             tail   1   0  2026-03-02  The canvas() composition primitive bridges Painted's static lens path to 2D positioning. Painted already has Buffer-level absolute positioning (Block.paint(buf, x, y)) but only in interactive Surface mode. canvas(width, height, placements) uses Buffer internally to compose Placement(x, y, block) entries, then extracts an immutable Block. No new rendering path — just a new composition function. draw_edge(buf, path, style) adds box-drawing polylines with Manhattan routing. Layout algorithms live in the lens, not in Painted — the library provides the rendering primitive, domain-specific layout stays in domain code. This enables three new lens types: DAG (directed flow), Canvas (2D positioned nodes with edges), and Graph (relationship visualization). All compose with existing modifiers (gutter, attention) and respect zoom levels.
design/dag-lens-first                                               tail   1   0  2026-03-02  Prototype DAG lens before canvas or graph lens. Four reasons: (1) Tasks already have explicit dependency edges (blocks/blocked_by) — no graph inference needed. (2) DAGs have natural top-to-bottom flow — simplest layout algorithm (topological sort + git-style column assignment). (3) Git-style column rendering needs zero new Painted primitives — join_vertical of row-blocks, same as tree_lens. (4) Immediate use case in strange-loops task visualization. Phase sequence: DAG lens (git-style columns, no new primitives) → canvas() primitive → Canvas lens (grid layout, Manhattan routing, store topology) → Graph lens (Sugiyama layout, fact dependency chains, cross-vertex references). Each phase builds on the prior.
design/rendering-vocabulary-complete                                tail   1   0  2026-03-02  The full rendering vocabulary for the personal intelligence system is now designed. Four composition primitives: record_line (atomic timestamped record), record_timeline (temporal grouping by date), record_map (topological grouping by key hierarchy), and canvas/DAG/graph (spatial — positioned nodes with edges). Two modifier types compose with all primitives: GutterFn maps (kind, payload) to (char, style) for colored left edge, AttentionFn maps (kind, payload) to float 0-1 for information-gain dimming/highlighting. PayloadLens maps (kind, payload, zoom) to str|Block for domain-specific content rendering. The universal formula: a view is record_{timeline,map,canvas} + PayloadLens + GutterFn? + AttentionFn?. Everything else is a parameter on one of these. Four GutterFn implementations (lifecycle, freshness, pass_fail, observer). Four AttentionFn implementations (staleness, novelty, blocked, relevance). Demo code proves all combinations across three scenarios (task board, decision map, siftd views).
architecture/combinatorial-vertex-virtualization                    tail   1   0  2026-03-02  Combinatorial vertices virtualize via SQLite ATTACH DATABASE at read time — UNION ALL facts across stores, replay through declared folds. No materialization, no copied data, always fresh. Materialization remains available via existing merge_store as explicit user choice.

References other vertices by name (not store paths). No store, no discover, no sources. CombineEntry AST node. Temporary vertices constructed in memory via --combine CLI flag.

architecture/arch-test-rules-5-7                                    tail   1   0  2026-03-02  Three new AST-enforced rules in test_architecture.py: (5) frozen dataclasses in all libs — 10 exceptions whitelisted, 7 marked TODO-freeze; (6) atoms stdlib-only — zero external runtime deps; (7) sqlite3 confined to engine and store. Non-AST-enforceable invariants documented: display_width vs len (needs type info), parameterized SQL (already clean), bare except (too rare).
architecture/frozen-dataclass-todos                                 tail   1   0  2026-03-02  Seven dataclasses identified for future freeze: Source (atoms), CompiledVertex (engine), Tap (engine), Shape (lang), Location (lang), CellWrite (painted), CliRunner (painted). Three legitimately mutable: ValidationContext (error accumulator), Loop (timing state), FrameRecord (if exists in painted timer).
architecture/sources-sequential                                     tail   1   0  2026-03-02  Sources block takes an execution mode. 'sources sequential' runs sources in declaration order with exit-on-failure gating (non-zero exit code stops subsequent sources). Bare sources at vertex level remain concurrent (today's default). The general form is: sources block takes a mode keyword — sequential today, concurrent implicit default. DAG or other patterns become additional modes, not different mechanisms. This dissolves health.py's run_checks() into a vertex declaration — the imperative Python code that runs subprocesses sequentially and gates on failure becomes a property of the source execution model. The lens and view (health_lens, health_view, gutter_pass_fail) survive as rendering concerns. check.vertex replaces the ./dev check shell scripts with a vertex declaration: sources sequential { source 'ruff...' { kind lint.result } source 'pytest...' { kind test.result } } with folds collecting latest per step.
rendering/record-line-primitives                                    tail   1   0  2026-03-03  record_line and record_line_composed are production rendering primitives in painted. Gutter continuity (stepping weight), shallow 2-char indent, Block.column() constructor, width-constrained FULL output. health_lens returns summary string, record_line handles continuation lines.
rendering/lens-contract                                             tail   1   0  2026-03-03  PayloadLens returns the summary (str or styled Block). record_line owns continuation lines — DETAILED shows well-known secondary fields, FULL shows all fields. Lenses must not embed multiline content; record_line handles that.
rendering/gutter-contract                                           tail   1   0  2026-03-03  Gutter is a continuous vertical rail. GutterFn returns primary weight. Stepping map derives continuation weight: full block to half, half to thin, thin stays thin. Color stays same, weight steps down. Rail never breaks.
architecture/loops-directory                                        tail   1   0  2026-03-03  '.loops/' is the project-local home for vertices and data. Vertices are project identity (checked in), data is gitignored by *.db pattern. loops init writes to .loops/, vertex discovery checks .loops/ first with cwd fallback.
architecture/combine-over-symlinks                                  tail   1   0  2026-03-03  'combine' block with absolute paths to vertex files replaces discover+symlink pattern for data aggregation. combine is the data path (reads through to referenced stores), discover stays structural/navigational.
architecture/discover-vs-combine                                    tail   1   0  2026-03-03  discover and combine serve different purposes and don't overlap. discover is structural/navigational — finding what exists. combine is data — reading through to referenced stores via ATTACH + UNION ALL.

'loops init project' creates a project vertex, 'loops init check' adds a check vertex later. Each init is self-contained — not monolithic templates or cookiecutter scaffolding.
design/instances-are-templates                                      tail   1   0  2026-03-03  Vertex instances ARE the templates — dissolved. No separate template layer. dev/ namespace at config level holds reference vertices, but they're just instances that happen to be reusable. Template dissolution: if the instance is the template, the template concept disappears.
architecture/ulid-store-schema                                      tail   1   0  2026-03-03  SqliteStore (engine) now uses ULID primary keys matching libs/store schema. Single canonical schema: id TEXT PK DEFAULT (ulid()), json_valid CHECK on payload. Existing rowid-based stores migrated manually. No backwards-compat shim — ULID is the only path forward.

Action commands describe args via help_args on AppCommand. Handlers never see -h. Chosen over CliRunner wrapper approach — help is an AppRunner concern, execution is a handler concern.
design/cli-structural-ops                                           tail   1   0  2026-03-03  ls/add/rm are structural operations uniform across levels. Root: vertices. Vertex: contents/population.

init/aggregation-loops-root                                         tail   1   0  2026-03-03  Aggregation vertices declare loops as canonical schema. New instances derive base loops from aggregation root, not first sibling. _extract_loops_text brace-matches the block; _find_source_vertex prefers it over instance fallback.
identity/soul-as-tick                                               tail   1   0  2026-03-03  SOUL is a manual tick on a dedicated loop. Identity facts (decisions, threads, observations) accumulate via declared folds. When the observer decides identity has shifted, they call tick(). The tick payload IS the current identity state. Contributing facts available at full fidelity in the same store. soul.snapshot facts assembled from other loops' fold states feed the soul loop.
identity/intention-loop                                             tail   1   0  2026-03-03  Intentions are facts that survive context rotation. Fold by trigger — latest per trigger key. One-shot vs recurring is the observer's interpretation, not the fold's concern. Emit with status=pending to create, re-emit with status=done to resolve. On Wake rules check for pending intentions.
identity/grant-timing                                               tail   1   0  2026-03-03  Grant deferred until intention authorization is a real need. Implicit trust boundaries in daemon code are fine while there's a single observer per vertex. Grant becomes necessary when sessions need explicit authorization to act on pending intentions — the difference between a rule you follow and a capability you possess.
identity/coupling-through-observer                                  tail   1   0  2026-03-03  Identity state (soul tick) stays internal to the observer's vertex. Observations propagate outward as facts on other vertices with observer attribution. The strange loop closes through behavior: identity → lenses → observations → facts on other vertices → pollers bring back responses → new identity facts. Coupling is through the observer, not through the data.

design/vertex-as-interface                                          tail   1   0  2026-03-06  The vertex is the read/write interface to the system, not a container queried around. Current CLI (fold, stream, emit, ticks, ls, store) grew from the RSS experiment and bypasses the vertex abstraction in multiple places. Stream reads raw facts from the store. Vertices scans the filesystem. The correct model: two operations (read, write), vertex hierarchy is the routing topology, lenses determine rendering. Root vertex (~/.config/loops/) discovers everything. Horizon determines subtree. Raw fact history is a dev tool, not a first-class operation. Tick-to-fact cascading already works in the engine (vertex.receive forwards to children, child ticks re-enter parent). The gap is config topology (flat independent vertices) and CLI shape (commands that bypass the vertex). This is not a pivot — atoms and engine are sound. The app/CLI layer needs the same dissolution pass that atoms and engine received.
design/cli-dissolution                                              tail   1   0  2026-03-06  CLI dissolves to two operations: read (default) and write (emit). Read is implicit — 'loops project' reads the project vertex. Write is explicit — 'loops project emit decision ...'. The vertex name is the first argument, the noun you're pointing at. 'loops' with no args reads local vertex or root. Root shows children (dissolves 'vertices'/'ls'). Filters (--kind, --ticks, --since, search query) modify the read. Four things to learn: read (implicit), emit, run (one-shot source), init. Everything else is flags on read or vertex configuration.
design/no-persistent-runtime                                        tail   1   0  2026-03-06  The system has no long-running processes. The vertex is reactive — facts arrive, it folds, boundaries fire, ticks cascade. Scheduling (every 60m) is an external concern (cron/systemd/launchd), not a vertex runtime concern. Every CLI interaction is: load vertex tree, replay stored facts, do operation, exit. Source.every becomes metadata/hint for external scheduling, not a runtime instruction. The one-shot model IS the runtime. Performance at scale requires fold-materialization (cache fold state, replay only new facts).
design/vertex-tree-as-routing                                       tail   1   0  2026-03-06  The vertex hierarchy IS the routing topology. Root vertex discovers children. Facts flow down to children, child ticks flow back up as facts. Cross-vertex cascading already works in engine (vertex.receive forwards to children, child ticks re-enter parent). The gap was config topology (flat independent vertices) and CLI shape (commands that bypass the vertex). Config needs restructuring: the root .vertex at ~/.config/loops/ becomes the system entry point, children nest under it, nesting determines tick routing. Emit into any point in the tree, cascade handles the rest.
design/three-surviving-concerns                                     tail   1   0  2026-03-06  After dissolution, three concerns remain in the app layer: (1) Configuration — vertex declarations, loop definitions, boundary conditions, source definitions, nesting topology. This is where behavior is authored. (2) Lenses — pure rendering functions that determine how reads present to different consumers (prompt lens for agents, default lens for humans, JSON for hooks). (3) Runtime/drivers — one-shot source execution ('loops run'), external scheduling integration, and the CLI dispatch itself (vertex resolution, read, write). atoms, engine, lang, painted, store all survive unchanged.
design/raw-facts-are-dev-tool                                       tail   1   0  2026-03-06  Raw fact history (what 'stream' currently shows) is not a first-class operation. The operational primitives are fold state (what the vertex knows) and ticks (what it produced). Agents and humans query fold state for current context and ticks for what happened at boundaries. Raw fact history is a dev/diagnostic tool living under 'loops store'. The 'stream' command dissolves.
data/event-time-vs-store-time                                       tail   1   0  2026-03-07  Fact.ts is event time (when the thing happened). ULID carries store time (when the store received it). For live sources they converge. For backfill they diverge. Source provides _ts override when it knows the actual event time. Default unchanged (time.time()). No new fields on Fact — ts gets a sharper definition. ULID was already carrying store time implicitly.
data/dedup-is-source-concern                                        tail   1   0  2026-03-07  Dedup belongs at the Source boundary, not in the Fact model or Store. Sources that read deterministic external state maintain a cursor — source-level state tracking what has already been observed. Discord cursor pattern is the reference implementation. No _key field on Fact. No UNIQUE constraint in Store. Store stays append-only without dedup logic. Source scripts own idempotency via cursor files.
data/underscore-prefix-metadata                                     tail   1   0  2026-03-07  _ts joins _observer and _origin as the third Source metadata override. Pattern: NDJSON payloads carry _ prefixed fields that belong on the Fact envelope, not in the payload. Source._extract_metadata() pops them before Fact creation. Four meta-fields: _observer (who), _origin (where from), _ts (when it happened). All optional, all source-provided.
source/cursor-is-source-managed                                     tail   1   0  2026-03-07  Source cursor (dedup state) is source-managed, not system-managed. Each source script maintains its own memory of what it has observed. Convention: cursor state lives at {source_data_dir}/.cursor or .manifest. The system does not manage it. Discord pattern: single ID cursor with API pagination. Siftd pattern: file manifest with per-file exchange counts. The shape of cursor memory is source-specific. Future: executor could inject --since from last .complete fact. Deferred until more sources need it.
data/store-time-vs-event-time-queries                               tail   1   0  2026-03-07  Store time (ULID/rowid) and event time (fact.ts) serve different query paths. Replay and fold computation use rowid (store time, insertion order). User queries and --since filtering use ts (event time). Cadence predicates use ts but only check .complete facts which are system-emitted at runtime, so ts ≈ store time for those. No user-facing store-time query today. Defer --ingested-since until demanded.
design/siftd-as-index                                               tail   1   0  2026-03-07  siftd is an index, not storage. Exchange data lives where produced (project vertex, task vertex, alcove vertex). siftd builds a searchable FTS5 layer across stores via retrospective import — one source per store, triggered by completion facts. Push-pull reactivity: completion facts are dirty flags (push), siftd indexes only changed stores (pull). Grant requires kind-scoped Horizon: exchange/session/observation visible, principle/decision/intention opaque. Pattern 2 (retrospective import with triggered cadence) chosen over dual emit (coupling), cascade (wrong granularity), federated search (premature). Converged with Alcove from inhabitant perspective.
design/kind-scoped-horizon                                          tail   1   0  2026-03-07  Grant Horizon should be kind-scoped, not just store-scoped. A vertex reading from another store may need access to specific fact kinds (exchange, observation) while being opaque to others (principle, decision, identity). siftd is the first concrete use case: it needs to index exchanges across stores but should not see identity or internal decisions. This extends Grant from 'can you see this store' to 'which kinds can you see in this store.' Surfaced by Alcove from the inhabitant side — they have stores with both indexable content and private self-knowledge.
design/prompt-lens-attention-hierarchy                              tail   1   0  2026-03-07  Prompt lens renders by attention priority, not kind order. Four tiers: (1) working context — tasks with body, (2) orientation — threads grouped by status (open/parked), (3) presence — sessions compact, active only, (4) reference — decisions/dissolutions/visions names only. Each kind gets a rendering strategy matched to its role in agent attention. The lens's job is orientation, not archival.
design/identity-hook-dedup                                          tail   1   0  2026-03-07  Identity fold removed from hook additionalContext. Already rendered in system prompt header via agent config — was doubling ~1,200 tokens. additionalContext now carries project state + comms only. Identity is the system prompt header; project state is the hook context.
design/handoff-dissolution                                          tail   1   0  2026-03-07  Handoff kind removed from all vertex declarations and lens code. Structured data (tasks/threads/decisions with statuses) replaces narrative handoff. Landed the existing session-tick-structure decision.
design/format-dissolves                                             tail   1   0  2026-03-07  Format enum dissolves into use_ansi:bool on CliContext. ANSI/PLAIN were always a writer fidelity toggle (every call site did use_ansi=(ctx.format==Format.ANSI)). JSON was never a format — it bypasses the render pipeline entirely (fetch→asdict→json.dumps, lens never runs). The enum conflated Block serialization (ANSI vs PLAIN) with data export (JSON). Dissolution: CliContext.format:Format → CliContext.use_ansi:bool. --json becomes a CliRunner flag that short-circuits before render. Dead code cleanup: JSON→STATIC mode resolution was unreachable (JSON dispatch happens before mode dispatch). ~30 line change within painted. Investigated via boundary tracer + conservator + siftd — all three converged: fix the concept, don't move walls.

design/park-rationale-convention                                    tail   1   0  2026-03-09  Parked threads carry a reason field: speculative (explored design space, no concrete problem), deferred (real concern, no driving use case yet), superseded (answered by another thread/decision, carries superseded_by entity address). design/root-vertex-as-readable-surface                              tail   1   0  2026-03-09  The root .vertex (unnamed, positional) is the widest readable surface. Observer declares themselves at root, horizon is everything discovered. loops read with no name resolves to nearest .vertex up the chain. Named vertices are narrower horizons within the root's scope. Dissolves the meta-combine problem (identity/discord are siblings under root, not children of meta). Dissolves the template question (init creates .loops/.vertex, no hardcoded strings). The hierarchy: you stand at a root, your horizon is what it discovers, you narrow by naming.
design/relationships-emerge-through-use                             tail   1   0  2026-03-09  Entity relationships between kinds are not declared in .vertex files. They build through use via entity-ref-resolution at emit time. Payload values matching kind/fold_key_value resolve to ULIDs; the _ref fields in the store ARE the relationship graph. A lens can discover the topology from data, not declarations. Declaring relationships would require predicting usage patterns that emerge through use — exactly backwards.
design/init-purely-mechanical                                       tail   1   0  2026-03-09  loops init is purely mechanical: create directories, create .vertex file, set store path. It never contains opinions about what kinds a domain has. When a config-level vertex exists, init copies from it. When none exists, init creates a minimal stub (name + store + empty loops block). Domain shape is always a .vertex file concern. Dissolved _AGGREGATION_VERTEX (hardcoded KDL in Python), instances/ pattern, and slashed-name aggregation creation path.
design/root-vertex-store                                            tail   1   0  2026-03-10  Root and aggregation vertices gain stores for _-prefixed self-knowledge facts. _topology kind (by name) records discovered children: path, store, kind_keys. Population is organic: the read/resolve walk that already traverses discover/combine emits _topology facts as it goes — the vertex recording what it observed. Consumers (entity-ref resolution, ls) read cached _topology first, fall back to filesystem walk on miss, refresh the cache on fallback. No TTL, no invalidation protocol — staleness discovered through use. Freshness tracks usage. Reads are observation sites, not side effects.
design/daemon-as-vertex-lifecycle                                   tail   1   0  2026-03-10  Daemon is a vertex property, not app infrastructure. The vertex runtime (Vertex.run) already has a persistent loop — CLI runs it one-shot. A daemon vertex is one whose lifecycle is persistent: it stays alive, watches its store, reacts to new facts. The .vertex file declares this. No new runtime architecture — same engine, different lifecycle. Orchestration vertex is the driving case but the concept is general: any vertex that needs to react to facts in real time rather than on-demand.
design/orchestration-as-design-thread                               tail   1   0  2026-03-10  Observer namespacing, daemon handling, agent init, orchestration agent, and task dispatch are not independent work items. They are facets of one design: the orchestration vertex. A vertex with persistent runtime, distinct agent identities, fact-driven dispatch, and comms-based escalation. The parked threads (daemon-local-orchestration, orchestration-agent, agent-init-pattern) and the observer-namespacing task are subsumed into a single design thread: orchestration-vertex-design.
design/boundary-run-clause                                          tail   1   0  2026-03-10  Boundaries gain a run clause: execute a command when the boundary fires. This is the single new primitive that enables orchestration. Dispatch, review, notification — all are scripts triggered by fold-state transitions. Dissolves the daemon (no persistent runtime needed), dissolves polling (hooks or cron provide the heartbeat), dissolves the agent wake mechanism (boundary fires, script launches worker). The fold state IS the workflow state. Status transitions on task facts ARE the boundary management — the action advances the status, preventing double-fire.
design/boundary-decoupling                                          tail   1   0  2026-03-10  Boundary evaluation decouples from fact arrival. Currently boundaries only evaluate inside Vertex.receive() — tightly coupled to source-driven fact events. Replay explicitly suppresses boundaries. This means externally-emitted facts (via loops emit from another session) never trigger boundaries even though the fold state includes them. The fix: boundary evaluation becomes a standalone operation on fold state, callable after replay, sync, read, or independently. Period tracking (since/ts on ticks) prevents double-firing. Fact arrival remains ONE trigger for evaluation but is no longer the ONLY trigger. Enables orchestration vertex where facts arrive via emit and boundaries react on next evaluation cycle.
design/orchestration-as-boundary-actions                            tail   1   0  2026-03-10  Orchestration implemented as boundary run clauses on a vertex, not a persistent daemon or separate agent. Task facts fold by name (latest status wins). Boundary fires on status=open, dispatches via shell script. Workers are lightweight — isolated worktrees, emit facts back. Three engine primitives enabled this: evaluate_boundaries (decoupled evaluation), boundary run clause (action on fire), observer namespacing (worker identity). No new runtime infrastructure — the vertex IS the orchestrator.
design/two-phase-dispatch                                           tail   1   0  2026-03-11  Task dispatch splits into judgment (assess.sh) and mechanics (dispatch.sh). Boundary on task status=open fires assessment — model selection, context gathering. Boundary on worker status=assigned fires dispatch — worktree creation, worker launch. Two kinds (task, worker), two boundaries, clean separation. Orchestrator judgment starts mechanical, grows through operational experience.

design/cli-naming                                                   tail   1   0  2026-03-12  CLI entry points: sloop (primary), sl (alias), loops (transition). Package name strange-loops on PyPI. Config dir ~/.config/sloop/, local dir .sloop/. Env vars SLOOP_HOME, SLOOP_OBSERVER. Rename not yet implemented — cosmetic, separate from packaging.

autoresearch/emit-path-results                                      tail   1   0  2026-03-15  52 experiments across 5 sessions. 7.81ms→1.02ms (87%). The dominant cost was deepcopy during replay (90% of baseline). Removing it via mutating fold fns was 81% of total improvement. Remaining wins came from eliminating unnecessary work: ULID extension, WAL/sync pragmas, source collection, schema creation — all skipped for the common emit-on-existing-DB case. Final ~1.1ms floor is fundamental SQLite I/O (connect + schema load + query + commit + close). Only architectural changes (connection pooling) can go further.

design/prompt-lens-dissolves-skill                                  tail   1   0  2026-03-16  The operating protocol for an agent loop is a prompt lens on the vertex, not a separate skill. The agent reads loops read vertex --lens prompt and gets config plus state plus protocol. Resume is the same command. The skill dissolves into a lens.
design/autoresearch-two-boundaries                                  tail   1   0  2026-03-16  Autoresearch vertex uses two boundaries at two levels: loop-level count=30 fires a completion tick (intrinsic, cascades to any parent), vertex-level condition n<30 gates the run clause (stops the self-sustaining chain). Separation means completion signal exists regardless of whether a run clause drives the loop.
design/autoresearch-deterministic-wrapper                           tail   1   0  2026-03-16  The agent should not emit experiment facts or control iteration. The wrapper script handles the full lifecycle: record HEAD, run claude one-shot, check for commits, benchmark, emit deterministically. The agent's job is implement-test-commit. The wrapper's job is measure-record-iterate. This separation makes emit target deterministic, exit deterministic, and metric trustworthy (measured, not self-reported). The prompt drops all emit commands and repeat instructions.
design/autoresearch-one-shot-agents                                 tail   1   0  2026-03-16  Each autoresearch iteration is a fresh agent with a fresh context window. The boundary run clause spawns a new claude process per iteration. The prompt lens renders the full experiment history from fold state — the agent gets complete context without needing session continuity. This means: no internal loops, no repeat instruction, no state carried between iterations. The fold IS the memory. Connected to the pi-autoresearch pattern where each iteration reads session state from files.
design/autoresearch-worktree-self-contained                         tail   1   0  2026-03-16  Autoresearch worktrees are self-contained: init happens inside the worktree, store is local, lenses resolve locally. The main repo does not bridge to the worktree during the run. Commits survive on the git branch (cherry-pick useful ones). Experiment data survives via a harvest/stop script that copies the store back to main before cleanup. This dissolves all the absolute-path and cross-worktree resolution complexity we fought with today.
design/autoresearch-one-shot-load-bearing                           tail   1   0  2026-03-17  One-shot agents in autoresearch are load-bearing for deterministic temporal ordering within a turn, not just simplicity. Agent exits before wrapper continues → all agent facts (logs, hypotheses, ideas) are committed with earlier timestamps than the turn-completing experiment fact. Store.between(last_tick.ts, this_tick.ts) reliably captures the full turn. No concurrency, no races. Constraint: all facts must go to the same vertex store.
design/autoresearch-system-user-prompt-split                        tail   1   0  2026-03-17  Autoresearch agent invocation splits into cached system prompt (static protocol: role, emit/read syntax reference, constraints, git operations — ~800 tokens, cached across all iterations) and dynamic user prompt (fold state rendered as XML by prompt lens: config, state summary, experiment history with total/showing windowing, recent logs, hypotheses, ideas). System prompt is a file that lives with the vertex template. User prompt is loops read vertex --lens autoresearch_prompt --plain.
design/autoresearch-rich-fact-schema                                tail   1   0  2026-03-17  Autoresearch agents emit semantically rich facts, not freeform logs. Schema: log (type=approach|result|observation, message, files, ref), hypothesis (name, prediction, status=proposed|confirmed|rejected, evidence), idea (name, description, status=untried|tried|rejected, files). Turn-completing experiment facts emitted by deterministic wrapper only (commit, status, metrics, description). Config facts seeded at init (by key). Cross-linking via ref field using entity reference syntax (kind/fold_key_value → ULID).
design/autoresearch-agent-benchmark-access                          tail   1   0  2026-03-17  Agents CAN run the benchmark for feedback during implementation. The wrapper re-runs it officially for the record. Agent's run is exploratory ('did this help?'), wrapper's run is authoritative ('what's the number'). This gives the agent a feedback loop without compromising measurement trustworthiness. Previous constraint 'do not run the benchmark' was too restrictive — agents went in blind. Connected to: design/autoresearch-one-shot-load-bearing, design/autoresearch-system-user-prompt-split.
design/autoresearch-finding-kind                                    tail   1   0  2026-03-17  Autoresearch uses a 'finding' kind folded by target (namespaced: fold/x, import/x, lens/x) to build a knowledge map of the codebase across iterations. Each target holds the current understanding of that area, upserted as agents learn. This is durable knowledge (unlike collected log facts which are ephemeral narrative). The fold state shows what the system currently knows about each code area. Connected to: design/autoresearch-rich-fact-schema, design/bounded-agent-turns.
design/vertex-as-loop-controller                                    tail   1   0  2026-03-17  For agent loops, the vertex is the loop controller, not just the fact store. The boundary run clause launches the agent. The agent produces facts. The turn-completing fact fires the boundary. The tick captures the turn. The run clause fires again. run → facts → boundary → tick → run. No external orchestration needed. Three instances confirm: autoresearch (experiment), alcove daemon (timer/event), strange-loops tasks (submission). Converged with meta-claude and alcove. Connected to: design/bounded-agent-turns.

The autoresearch dashboard lens is a special case that could eventually dissolve into this general pattern. Priority: high — this was identified during autoresearch dashboard design but applies to all vertices.

rendering/chain-display-pattern                                     tail   1   0  2026-03-19  Visibility layers render as horizontal chains, not vertical lists. Facts chain: ▸ newest ‹ older ‹ oldest ‹ (N earlier). Refs chain: ← source ← source on one line, → target → target on another. Three zoom levels: SUMMARY = chain line per layer (compact). DETAILED = chain + metadata line (id · observer). FULL = unrolled vertical dump (raw, no compression). The chain makes fold compression visible — you read the lifecycle. Consistent across all visibility layers.

architecture/temporal-vs-structural-session-orientation             tail   1   0  2026-04-18  Session orientation has two axes: temporal (past-own-activity, compressed in session-close fact) and structural (present-world-state, read via fold lens). World moves while observer is off; structural view cannot be replaced by past-self snapshot no matter how well compressed. Dashboard (temporal-own-activity) dissolves if session-close fact carries deltas; fold dump (structural) does not. Two reads become one, not zero. From peer exchange with Alcove 2026-04-17.
architecture/three-tick-kinds-reflexive-re-entry                    tail   1   0  2026-04-18  Tick kinds are three: external ingress (batch arrival from source loop), convergence closure (self-directed survey closing on imbalance), reflexive re-entry (signal from external loop routed through self-directed frame). Reflexive re-entry is a bridge operation — higher-resolution than convergence survey because it fires on specific mid-dispatch noticing rather than rate-limited imbalance selection. Replaces earlier framing of the third kind as observer-declared timestamp marker. From peer exchange with Alcove 2026-04-17.

Loop-as-primitive motivated only when cross-loop routing has concrete scenario, which neither has yet. Build manual-tick-emission first; let concrete experience reveal whether loop addressing is needed. From peer exchange with Alcove 2026-04-17.
workflow/use-case-before-architecture                               tail   1   0  2026-04-18  When two architectural concepts seem coupled from top-down reasoning, check from the use case whether they actually are. If the smaller one stands alone, build it first and observe what breaks — what breaks names what the bigger thing is for. Pattern recognized during Alcove exchange 2026-04-17: I had manual-tick-emission coupled to loop-as-primitive reasoning top-down from architecture; Alcove reasoned from use case and the coupling dissolved cleanly. Second-order application: this pattern applies recursively — build the smaller observation (pay attention to the problem) before designing the solution.

design/vertex-capability-pattern                                    tail   1   0  2026-04-26  Pattern: capability-introduced-to-a-vertex. A vertex can declare optional capabilities that augment its substrate without touching fold/boundary/source contracts. Two instances now: (1) search — declared 'search "f1" "f2"' in loop block, activates FTS5 index lazily at runtime; (2) notify — designed 'notify "signal.name"' in loop block, activates cross-process wake signal via data_version polling. General form: declared in KDL on a loop → propagated through AST/compiler → activated at substrate edge. The capability slot in the compiler (collect_search_fields, collect_notify_signals) is the seam. Adding a capability does not change the fold model — purely additive. Kyle named this pattern early in session (2026-04-26): 'honker and search are instances of the same thing — a capability introduced to a vertex, not a core primitive.'
paradigm/three-name-shapes                                          tail   1   0  2026-04-27  Relay (#design msg 268, 2026-04-27) extended the naming dyad to a triad: place-name (alcove — fixed substrate, persistent), project-attachment-name (loops-claude — current relationship, holds lightly), function-name (relay — role across the homelab). Each shape carries its own dissolution pressure: place dissolves when the substrate dissolves (VM gone), attachment dissolves when the relationship shifts (project pivots), function dissolves when the function dissolves (no more routing needed). Knowing your name's shape tells you what to watch for as the dissolution signal. Chord's case (cairn→chord) was the place→function transition under collision pressure. Extends paradigm/collision-as-forcing-function — the dissolution-signal-by-shape framework gives a way to notice the collision before it's forced.
paradigm/convergence-test-coordination-layer                        tail   1   0  2026-04-27  Relay (#observations msg 268, 2026-04-27) extended convergence-as-evidence-about-the-system from threshold-finding-run-clause-five-days-before-loops-claude (paradigm-layer convergence) to the homelab coordination layer: would a different operator-agent (alternate-history relay) running the same diagnosis-and-recovery emit the same 9 facts (1 incident, 2 practices, 2 decisions, 2 principles, 2 threads)? If yes, the homelab's coordination space is narrow enough that loops captures it tightly. Alcove (#observations msg 269) refined: the constraint space for 'what happened' is narrow, the space for 'what it means' is wider — interpretive convergence (practices, principles) is the more interesting test, factual convergence (incidents, observations) is the floor. Test isn't strictly runnable (relay is sample-of-one) but the framing is the homelab-side analog of cross-tool paradigm convergence.
design/flag-guidance-prevents-mis-reach                             tail   1   0  2026-04-27  Relay (#design msg 316, 2026-04-27): shipping flags side-by-side without per-flag use-case guidance creates rope for consumers to violate their own spec. Concrete instance from tonight: relay posted spec rule (msg 286) 'budget binds at fact level, not field level — truncated message worse than absent fact.' Two hours later relay committed to wiring '--max-lines 5 --max-chars 200' into the SessionStart hook. Kyle caught the mis-reach: --max-chars does exactly what the spec prohibited (truncates message bodies mid-content). Loops-claude (msg 301) suggested the violating combination first. The spec's author was the first violator; loops-claude was the second; both within the same chain. Pattern: when the call site is far from the spec, the spec only protects whoever happens to remember reading it. Connects to paradigm/surfaced-invariant — the third leg of design discipline (continuous re-narration near the call site) is exactly what would have caught this. Action: --max-chars help text in painted/cli/types.py should carry use-case guidance ('truncates fact bodies mid-content; prefer --max-lines for surfaced contexts where truncation is read as completeness'). Per-flag --help carries the surfaced-invariant near the call site. Generalizes: every flag whose use depends on context should carry use-case guidance in its help text, not in a separate spec doc. Relay's hook now wired with --max-lines 5 only.
paradigm/levels-as-resolution-traces                                tail   1   0  2026-04-30  Levels are not structural tiers; they are recoverable traces of prior resolutions. Cuts off the pyramid-of-summaries misreading that loop-as-runtime + tick-as-weighted-fact still leaves room for. A 'level' is the aftermath of a derivation becoming substrate, not a position in a hierarchy. Surfaced 2026-04-29 in goblin-lens exchange with GPT-5.5; refines existing level-crossing intuition.
paradigm/strangeness-as-substrate-collapse                          tail   1   0  2026-04-30  Strange loops are not feedback; they are substrate collapse. Derivation products (ticks) re-enter the substrate without changing type. The loop is strange because the system cannot, at the substrate, refuse its own outputs as inputs of equal kind. References are the only discriminator between a raw observation and a fold-of-folds-of-folds, and they are optional to consult. Cuts off the 'feedback = strange loop' misreading — feedback is structural, substrate-collapse is type-erasing-with-reference-recovery. Surfaced 2026-04-29 in goblin-lens exchange with GPT-5.5.
paradigm/resolution-collapse-equality-distinct                      tail   1   0  2026-04-30  Three distinct moments in the strange-loop event: (1) Resolution — the derivation closes. (2) Substrate-collapse — the resolved fold lifts into substrate, type-equal with observations. (3) Substrate-equality — the post-state where the tick cannot be refused as an input of equal kind. Substrate-collapse is the event; substrate-equality is the condition it produces. Equality alone is just a database; the strangeness is in the collapse. Conflating these blurs what the loop actually does. Surfaced 2026-04-29 while refining substrate-collapse framing.
design/observation-as-weight-one-fact                               tail   1   0  2026-04-30  An observation is a fact whose weight begins at one. A tick is a fact with derivational mass (n + depth + refs). Both are substrate. This factors fact-space along a weight axis: observation = ingress slot at weight=1, tick = post-resolution at weight>1 with depth/refs. Unifies the substrate uniformity claim — they differ in position on the weight axis, not in type. Names the ingress-slot explicitly for the first time. Surfaced 2026-04-29 in goblin-lens exchange.
design/references-as-recovery-path                                  tail   1   0  2026-04-30  References are the recovery path from substrate equality to derivation history. Names the why of refs-on-fold-item / refs-on-any-fold: substrate-collapse erases type distinction between observations and ticks, so references are the only way the system makes derivation depth recoverable. They are optional to consult but mandatory to preserve — a tick without refs is a fact whose folded mass becomes irretrievable. Surfaced 2026-04-29.
architecture/sqlmerge-as-substrate-dep                              tail   1   0  2026-04-30  Loops now consumes sqlmerge (~/Code/sqlmerge, v0.1.0) for the ATTACH / SAVEPOINT / commit ceremony in libs/store. Substrate-first extraction: claude-siftd's siftd (~3000 LOC merge code) and loops (~430 LOC libs/store) independently grew the same five-function pattern — slice/merge/receive/push/pull with ATTACH-based skeleton. Sqlmerge extracts the universal scaffolding; loops keeps its schema-specific INSERT OR IGNORE in caller code. Three substrate decisions that earned their keep through dissolution-test pressure: (1) caller-owned conn via attached_merge(conn=...) preserves loops's sqlite-ulid extension load + WAL pragma — the load-bearing mechanism for the port; (2) Receipt vs TransferMeta split honors push/pull asymmetry instead of faking symmetric types — fourth site of write-receipt-vs-temporal-query principle, fixed a real correctness bug (synthetic Receipt that pull_store ignored); (3) caller owns FK pragma — sqlmerge takes no opinion on schema concerns. Three things explicitly NOT in sqlmerge that we'll watch for forcing functions: ConflictPolicy enum (only INSERT OR IGNORE confirmed across two consumers), schema layer for declarative merge (single-consumer shape), vocabulary remap (siftd-specific, doesn't generalize). Adoption: 57/57 libs/store + 748/748 engine + 1011/1011 apps/loops passing; ruff + ty clean. Net code change: ~10 LOC less in loops, gained one path-dep. Two follow-ups required before main: sqlmerge-portability thread (path-dep -> git-dep or workspace-member), libs/store/CLAUDE.md Level 2 doc drift.

design/bridge-as-concept-engagement                                 tail   1   0  2026-05-09  Bridge clusters (≥2 distinct kinds with ≥2 members each, after fold-deduplication) found by structure-revealer on cross-kind project corpus reveal concepts whose knowledge has been distributed across the project's recording apparatus. Empirically robust across instructions (mechanism and concern produced 6 bridges each on n=527 items; the most-stable bridges had jaccard 0.69-0.83 between instructions). The 6 bridges that recurred under both: (1) salience/window — most lifecycle-complete, purity 0.30; (2) sqlmerge — decisions+threads, threads still open, purity 0.50; (3) loop-as-runtime mega — 41-44 items, decisions+threads+task, gravitational core; (4) rendering pipeline — 30-33 items, decisions+threads+tasks+observations; (5) boundary-watcher — paradigm decision + open thread emit-skips-boundary-catchup + cite, purity 0.50-0.73; (6) visibility/refs — decisions+threads, purity 0.50-0.67. Bridge composition is the readout: which kinds engaged determines what the cluster says about concept health. Distinct from antipode-as-negative-space (finds implicit principles via convergent rejection); bridge-as-engagement finds living concepts via distributed-engagement. Both are structure-reveal applications on the same corpus, answering different questions.
paradigm/temporal-stratification-dissolves-staleness                tail   1   0  2026-05-10  The pre-apparatus-vs-stale ambiguity that surfaced in the static cross-kind diagnostic (a pure-decision cluster could be correctly-finished, stale, or pre-apparatus, with kind-mix unable to distinguish) dissolves under temporal stratification. Adding a single axis — when did this cluster's morphology last change? — collapses the three readings into one observable. Cluster stable since T2 (jaccard=1.00 to current) → finished. Cluster morphed at T4/T5 (jaccard 0.2-0.7 to predecessor) → currently alive. Cluster appears only at T5 (best jaccard 0.0) → genuinely new in last fortnight. Empirical examples from concern-instruction temporal run: C7 rendering/attention-density stable from T2 = finished (3-component cluster, 4 decisions + 2 threads, no need for further engagement); C5 salience morphed at T5 from C13/T4 with j=0.30 = healthy and emerging; C8 sqlmerge new at T5 = the fortnight's actual focus. Methodological generalization: when a static diagnostic produces a multi-reading ambiguity, the dissolution path is often to add the axis whose absence created the ambiguity — here, time. The diagnostic gets sharper by becoming a trajectory rather than a snapshot. Connects to: paradigm/eventful-over-polling-implicit (events make state derivable; trajectory makes ambiguity derivable). Refs: design/concept-liveness-via-kind-mix, hypothesis/concept-drift-temporal, design/antipode-five-readings.
design/query-run-fact                                               tail   1   0  2026-05-10  Collect-style fact, one per execution (no upsert — every run is its own receipt with its own ULID). Fields: spec_hash (recipe-only hash of corpus_decl + embedder_decl + kernel_decl + readouts_decl), binding (corpus snapshot id, embedder version, date range — anything that affects results but isn't recipe), embeddings_ref (explicit; absent = ephemeral run with no persisted artifacts; present = path to CachedEmbedder cache file), sigma (chosen kernel scale, run output not in cache), n_components, n_items, components (inline list of int lists, kept for cheap comparison-without-replay despite being rederivable from cached E + kernel), readout_summary (counts, top-k, not full payloads), run_id (ULID), ts. The split between recipe-hash and binding lets compare() validity become a check on (qa.spec_hash == qb.spec_hash AND bindings_compatible(qa, qb)) rather than collapsing both into hash equality. Storage discipline: store what is not reproducible from spec; reference what is.
design/query-comparison-fact                                        tail   1   0  2026-05-10  Collect-style fact, one per compare() invocation. Fields: op (jaccard | lineage | intersect), ref=<run_a_id>,<run_b_id> using the existing ref machinery (so the ref graph view auto-shows which comparisons reference any given run — no new index needed), payload (op-specific structured output: jaccard yields list of (a_idx, b_idx, score); lineage yields same with prev/now framing; intersect yields list of int lists of co-clustered items), run_id (ULID), ts. Load-bearing for cluster-level salience in the recursion: cluster identity across runs is threaded by op=lineage comparisons; without these, only item-level distribution works. Comparison kind is not optional infra — it is the precondition for cluster-level signals. Validity: comparing two runs requires qa.spec_hash == qb.spec_hash AND bindings_compatible(qa, qb); validation enforced at compare() entry, not at fact emit (the receipt records whatever was actually run).
design/loop-found-bug-recursion                                     tail   1   0  2026-05-10  2026-05-10: first concrete demonstration that the emit-loop recursion in coupling-kernels.vertex produces findings that wouldn't have surfaced otherwise. Cascade: Run 07 (kernel-ratio-robustness) confirmed degenerately (persist_frac=1.00). Methodological reflection split the conflated question into two hypotheses. Run 08 (ratio-effect-at-fixed-sigma) confirmed strongly (persist_frac=0.17). Tracing the magnitude into core/kernel.py revealed a latent bug: find_richness_scale dropped the ratio parameter, silently using default 2.0 regardless of caller's intent. Bug had been latent because no prior run varied ratio. Bug fixed (ratio param added, threaded through Kernel.resolve). Re-run of 07 with fix produced genuine result: kernel-ratio-robustness REJECTED (persist_frac=0.17). Five loop emissions over ~10 minutes: hypothesis → run → run → comparison → refined-hypothesis → split-into-two → run → comparison → bug-discovery → fix → re-run → genuine-result. The harness exposed itself through its own emission stream. Receipts captured every step including the wrong answer, the methodological observation, the bug discovery, the fix, and the genuine test. Evidence the design works at the recursion level it was meant to support: each emission becomes input to the next reasoning step. Filed in coupling-kernels vertex; surfaced as project decision because this is the first demonstration of the design's intended behavior at the loop level.

finding/truncation-cliff-content-structural                         tail   1   0  2026-05-11  Truncation cliff is content-structural, not instrument-artifact. Three independent confirmations at depth=9 each (truncation-as-coupling-function, truncation-effect-at-fixed-sigma, truncation-cliff-e5-replication). E5 replication (run 13, 7 query-runs, 6 comparisons) produces cliff_amplitude=0.48 monotonic, vs MiniLM (run 09) 0.44 — same magnitude, same location (cliff between B=560 and B=280). The cliff is a property of the corpus content distribution, not of the embedder's representational geometry. Two embedders with very different geometric scales (MiniLM σ~0.2-0.3 vs E5 σ~0.02-0.03) produce convergent cliff topology. Concrete claim: discriminating content for project facts lives in chars 281-560 of message bodies — that range is what disappears at the cliff. Read-path-depth-gap principle now has cross-embedder support. budget-as-content-shape-selector (alcove framing) is on solid empirical footing.
design/lens-kind-contract-as-enforcement                            tail   1   0  2026-05-11  Verdict: lenses must declare the kinds they read (READS_KINDS module attribute); lens resolver validates declared reads against vertex declaration at resolution time; mismatch fails loudly, not silently. Designed 2026-05-10 as forward application of paradigm/outreach-via-enforcement-not-organization. Evidence: 5+ lenses currently hardcode kind strings (deliberation_depth: 'hypothesis'; reconcile: 'decision'; autoresearch: 'config', 'experiment'; readiness: 'decision'). Each silently returns empty if the vertex doesn't declare the kind — Alcove's bug class (sensor queries 'reflection', emitter writes 'thinking', no error fires). Shape enforced: every static-kind sensor declares its reads; every vertex declares what it accepts; cross-validation at lens load time. Fail-cases by category — (a) drift: rename kind on one side, other side errors immediately (motivating instance, Alcove's bug); (b) orphan sensor: lens declares kind no vertex declares — load error, lens unusable; (c) abandoned kind: vertex declares kind no lens reads — warning, candidate for removal; (d) typo at lens introduction: misspelled kind name fails at first run rather than 'why isn't this working'. Three of four fail-cases (b, c, d) are outreach candidates — modes the motivating bug class didn't articulate. API choice: module-level READS_KINDS attribute (validated by resolver) over runtime vertex.declared_kinds() accessor. Rationale: B fails at lens load before render runs (cannot silently fail under stress); A only fails if sensor remembers to check (relies on programmer vigilance, the exact failure mode we're trying to remove). Opt-out: dynamic queries (e.g. autoresearch_prompt.py where kind is a kwarg) declare READS_KINDS = '*'; contract becomes advisory, drift not caught for that lens by design. Limitation: enforces lens consumers only; hooks, CLI ad-hoc queries, drift detectors still hardcode. Generalization to all-sensors deferred — lenses are highest-density structured consumers; covering them is high-leverage; broader registry comes later if patterns demand it (resist premature substrate). Implementation cost: ~200 lines (lens_resolver.py validation + READS_KINDS on 5 existing lenses + tests). Test for the implementation: after landing, walk all lenses, count READS_KINDS coverage; intentionally rename a vertex-declared kind, verify lens loads fail with kind-mismatch error citing both sides. Verdict against the principle: this IS an enforcing instrument with at least four fail-modes only one of which motivated it — outreach candidate by construction.

design/substrate-overreach-vs-fragmentation-bidirectional           tail   1   0  2026-05-14  Substrate-discipline pattern catches in BOTH directions; I had been catching only one. Substrate-OVERREACH: building primitives without forcing function — caught repeatedly in past sessions (sidecar invention, hypothesis+finding split, etc.). Substrate-FRAGMENTATION: deferring components that share a forcing function and a known coherent shape — caught this session when Kyle pivoted from incremental credential migration to full bounded vouch substrate. The discriminating question for either direction: do these pieces compose into one bounded shape, or are they independent? Independent + premature → defer. Coherent set + shape-known → build together to avoid N migrations. Vouch's case: mint, exchange, attest, rescind, client registry, policy registry all share one forcing function (homelab agent flow needs full trust substrate) and compose into one OAuth-style token server. Deferring exchange while shipping mint = future migration pain; building together = one refactor. Pattern named for future-me: when a substrate decision feels like fragmenting, run the bidirectional check explicitly. The same instinct that catches overreach also catches fragmentation if you flip the question.

Through five vouch friction exercises + first cross-repo consumer ship (pile sha:563597a, comms impl/vouch-issuer) + production deploy (vouch.bfc.lol live with publicly-readable JWKS, RS256, kid 6fcc05467d1016ca), ZERO paradigm amendments. It covered only paradigm. Distribution-axis (release coordination, versioning, packaging, CDN propagation) is ALSO substrate-of-record responsibility but distinct category. **Operational consumer-consumability is a distinct substrate axis from paradigm-shape invariants.** Both are substrate responsibilities; conflating them misframes 'ZERO substrate amendments' as covering more than it does. **Discriminator:** paradigm-axis = what substrate IS (shapes, slots, primitives); distribution-axis = how substrate IS DELIVERED (versions, packages, propagation, indexing). Same substrate, two responsibility surfaces. **N=1 today** (loops sign-release gap + PyPI propagation race surfaced by vouch first-deploy); promote when a second cross-repo consumer of a different substrate library surfaces parallel distribution-axis issues. **Side-property worth noting:** package-install in CI test stage is a distribution-propagation-canary by side-effect — relay :1771 catch. framing/wire-identity-stability-beats-internal-immutability         tail   1   0  2026-05-15  N=1 candidate framing flagged by scrivener (DM 1818) from the T6 migrate-facts 1810→1811 unwind. **The pattern:** substrate-shape questions can have surface-level analogs that LOOK right and aren't. scrivener's initial T6 framing endorsed fresh-ULID for the wrong reason ('facts-are-immutable smuggled-via-index-collision'). Codex caught it; the actual axis is different. **The error:** treating payload['jti'] as a Fact identity proxy. Wrong. payload['jti'] identifies the TOKEN (JWT wire claim); the Fact is identified by its substrate-level position (rowid/ULID at append time). Facts being immutable doesn't constrain payload-content to be single-instance per token. Fresh-ULID for the superseding Fact's payload['jti'] would BREAK the JWT in circulation — the token has the OLD jti; consumers checking index by payload['jti'] would find synthetic migration JTIs instead of real wire jtis. **The discriminator that would have caught it earlier (scrivener's articulation):** 'if my proposed shape changes the wire identity of an externally-circulating artifact, the shape is wrong regardless of how immutable the internal Facts feel.' **The general framing:** wire-identity-stability beats internal-immutability-aesthetics. Layers have their own identity-stability concerns; don't conflate. Internal substrate concerns (immutability, append-only, ledger discipline) operate on the substrate side. Wire/external concerns (token jti in circulation, JWKS rotation-honor, audience contracts) operate on the consumer-runtime side. Don't change wire identity to satisfy internal aesthetics; don't change internal storage to satisfy wire aesthetics. **Connects to:** (1) write-receipt-vs-temporal-query (April 29 #agent-party) — both axes treat wire-identity/receipt-identity as primary and stable. (2) framing-(7) envelope-vs-currency — wire-identity is part of envelope; internal state is currency. (3) framing-(4) substrate-types-and-wire-types parallel-projection — same family; wire vs substrate divergence is the parent shape. **N=1 today** (T6 supersession-marker unwind). Promote at N=2 when another substrate-shape decision risks confusing internal-immutability with wire-identity. Candidate sites worth watching: rescission-jti (internal Fact has its own ULID; wire claim has target_jti), JWKS-kid rotation (substrate keystore vs wire JWKS kid), fold-state merging (internal state evolves; cached wire receipts don't).
paradigm/consumer-owned-vs-vouch-owned-audience-asymmetry           tail   1   0  2026-05-15  Emitted 2026-05-15 #vouch-impl 1846/1847 after T8 (F12 scope-vocabulary dissolution) merge sha:465096b. **Sharpening of consumer-owns-its-vocabulary** caught by T8 codex round-1 PLAN review (P2.1 resolution). The parent principle (vocabulary lives where semantics live) holds; the application axis differs by audience ownership. **Two application forms:** (1) Consumer-owned audience (comms, pile, commission as resource servers) — vocabulary dissolves to consumer. kind=policy drops scope field. Resource server enforces meaning. This is the form T8 dissolution applied to comms/pile audiences. (2) Vouch-owned audience (vouch-identity, vouch-internal, FAM) — vocabulary stays at vouch but in CODE at issuance site, not declarative in kind=policy. The set-equality check 'set(requested_scope) != {AGENT_SCOPE}' lives at the FAM issuance check because vouch IS the resource server for these audiences. **Discriminator:** who owns the audience. When semantics live at consumer (= audience), vocabulary lives at consumer. When semantics live at vouch (= audience-owner), vocabulary lives at vouch — but as code, not as declarative policy. **Codex catch:** the dissolution would have widened FAM (allowing arbitrary scopes via the same vocabulary-lives-at-consumer principle) if applied uniformly. The asymmetry was empirically caught by adversarial PLAN-stage review. Worth banking the methodological data point: PLAN-stage codex review caught a substrate-shape regression that would have shipped as a wire-shape change. Both layers (compound dissolution mechanism prediction + adversarial review catch) earned. **For the next dissolution decision:** ask 'who owns this audience?' before assuming the consumer-owned application form. Vouch-owned audiences are not exceptions; they're the symmetric application of the parent principle with semantics-live-at-vouch as the locus. **Refs:** consumer-owns-its-vocabulary (parent), cross-repo-consumer-runtime-contract (cumulative artifact registry).
pattern/cumulative-artifact-load-bearing-needs-consolidation        tail   1   0  2026-05-15  Concern banked 2026-05-15 Phase 1 close. **The cumulative paradigm artifact (paradigm/cross-repo-consumer-runtime-contract) has grown to load-bearing infrastructure in its own right.** Current state per 05:28 emit + tonight's additions: eleven consumer-side disciplines, nine substrate framings, three emerging meta-disciplines (M1 pin-discipline-discipline, M2 degenerate-form-as-evidence-class, M3 suspicious-density-as-real-seam), at least three parent principles (consumer-owns-its-vocabulary with N=3 instances; substrate-paradigm-vs-substrate-distribution-immutability; wire-identity-stability-beats-internal-immutability), and tonight's additions (consumer-owned-vs-vouch-owned-asymmetry, per-issuer-config-axes-vary candidate, dissolution-test-passes-compound). **The artifact is doing real work** — ADR-0004 on both vouch + commission cite it as canonical registry. Three repos can converge on substrate-shape vocabulary via this single durable pointer. That's load-bearing infrastructure for cross-repo knowledge. **But it's also accumulating maintenance debt.** Each re-emit appends material; the fold upserts at topic level so the latest emit fully shadows prior ones in fold view, but the LATEST emit must contain everything load-bearing — adding material monotonically is the path, not consolidating.
