design/observer-string-trust-load-bearing-only-locally              tail   1   0  2026-05-16  Substrate invariant named explicitly 2026-05-15 (Kyle): the observer field on a Fact is a trustworthy attribution string ONLY when the emit happens on a machine the receiver controls. Currently implicit and breaks silently. Cross-machine emit can lie about observer; nothing in the system complains. The fact silently encodes wrong attribution. auth_emit/gated_receive is the cryptographic backing that makes the invariant hold off-machine. Local-emit stays string-only (cheap, trusted-by-locality); cross-wire emit MUST go through auth_emit or its attribution is unsigned-claim, not attestation. This was the discomfort Kyle had been carrying about scaling beyond local — now named.
design/validator-tick-equals-audit-record                           tail   1   0  2026-05-16  Further dissolution of validator-lambda case under tick-equals-fact universalism: on completion, the boundary fires a tick — that tick IS the audit record. No separate audit-emission concern. Local store ephemeral (CloudWatch log-of-facts, retention=14d); remote store receives either the tick-as-fact (with full-fidelity payload including all contributing facts) OR the slice-of-bytes (raw facts) — both shapes work, choice is per-deployment. Stratified-retention pattern handles local/remote split. No new primitives needed. The validator case is just: accumulate facts, fire boundary on completion, let the existing transport+retention machinery handle the rest.
design/slice-with-ref-closure-as-loops-primitive                    tail   1   0  2026-05-16  Loops primitive surfaced 2026-05-15 (Kyle caught the slice/transport conflation): ref-following belongs in slice, not transport. Slice decides WHAT to extract (kinds, time, observers, refs); transport moves whatever bytes slice produces. Architectural separation already in libs/store; ref-closure is a slice extension. Proposed shape: slice_store(source, target, *, kinds=[...], since=..., follow_refs=True) — when follow_refs=True, scan included facts for ref-fields (cred_ref, ref=*, any kind:fold_key references), include referenced facts as dependency-closure. Generic substrate capability: useful anywhere cross-vertex referencing matters (cred_ref for vouch lineage; entity-ref for the existing ref machinery; future use cases not yet named). Vouch is the FIRST motivating consumer, not the owner. Transport remains pluggable Protocol with push/pull — unchanged. Whether to follow_refs is per-slice policy, not per-transport policy. The 'lineage survives transport' property in vouch's case becomes 'slice with follow_refs=True produces self-contained bundles.'
design/friction-as-fact-kind                                        tail   1   0  2026-05-16  Friction is its own first-class fact kind, distinct from thread and task. Discriminating property: friction = "behavior I want but tooling/structure makes hard, with a specific fix in mind." Distinct from thread (open conversation/arc, scope-to-determine) and task (one-shot tracked work). Status lifecycle: open / in_progress / resolved / parked. Fold key: name=. Enables: queryable backlog via `sl read project --kind friction`, runbook-aligned discipline (Kyle leans on it heavily), discriminated from generic threads. Rationale for not dissolving into thread: friction has specific shape (deters a behavior + has a fix) that thread does not — and the backlog-scan use case wants kind-filter, not topic-prefix-filter. atoms/walked-items-as-foldstate-extension                           tail   1   0  2026-05-17  A2 of trace-dissolution: FoldState gains a parallel walked: tuple[WalkedItem, ...] field. Decision: separate the walked entities from primary sections rather than mutating FoldItem or hacking section.kind. RATIONALE: (a) FoldItem is widely consumed by lenses (prompt, gist, fold-view, painted record_line, etc.) — adding _via_anchor/_depth metadata bleeds into all of them and risks walked items being rendered as primary by lenses that do not check the metadata; (b) hacking section.kind to "walked-from-X" breaks kind-based dispatch in every lens consumer; (c) per-anchor map (dict[anchor, list]) loses iteration order and requires the lens to maintain anchor→items joins. The flat parallel tuple is opt-in: lenses that ignore .walked keep working unchanged; lenses that render the walk look at it explicitly. SHAPE: WalkedItem(item: FoldItem, section_kind: str, via_anchor: str, via_direction: str = "outbound", depth: int = 1). Default direction outbound (A2 walks ref= forward only — inbound walk deferred until evidence shows it is needed). depth=1 for direct refs of any primary anchor, depth=2 for refs-of-refs, etc. via_anchor is the kind/key address of the entity whose ref pulled this in (for depth=2, this is a depth-1 entity, not the original primary anchor — preserves the lineage chain for the ↳ nesting render). CYCLES: walked entities whose address (section_kind/key) already appears in the primary sections are not added to walked (avoid rendering the anchor twice). Walked entities that point back to other already-walked entities can dim or omit per render policy. BACK-COMPAT: FoldState.walked defaults to empty tuple — no fetch path is required to populate it; only fetch_fold(refs_depth>0) will. All existing consumers ignore .walked unchanged.

design/sub-namespace-under-add                                      tail   1   0  2026-05-17  Phase 2 verb-collision resolution. Decision: 'loops add <vertex> <subcommand>' shape with explicit subcommand keyword (kind | observer | combine | row). Rationale (Kyle's framing): lists are in KDL too, so 'add' uniformly means 'add an entity to a vertex' and the subcommand specifies WHICH entity-shape. Reads consistently: add row to population, add kind to loops block, add observer to observers block, add combine entry to combine block. Bare-positional 'loops add reading X Y' preserved as implicit row for back-compat; Phase 3 will retire it alongside the rss-era surface. Rejected alternatives: (a) flag-driven disambiguation on 'add' (--kind X vs positional X Y) — brittle to typos like --kibd silently falling through to row mode; (b) new verb 'declare' or 'def' — clean but creates two verbs for the same conceptual operation (extending the vertex). The chosen shape generalizes to Phase 3+ when more subcommands land (template, sources, lens, boundary).

design/fold-off-type-skip-with-counter                              tail   1   0  2026-06-12  R2 RESOLVED (Kyle, 2026-06-12): an off-type value in a numeric fold (Sum/Avg/Min/Max/TopN-by) is SKIPPED — no state mutation, Avg denominator untouched — and recorded in a deterministic {target}_rejected counter in fold state. Bool is off-type (Python bool-is-int silently folded true as 1). Latest joins the rule: missing _ts rejects, NEVER falls back to time.time() (replay determinism). Missing field stays silent-skip (absence is not an error); off-type presence is. Errors-as-state over errors-as-facts: visible in every snapshot, zero new machinery, no write-on-read, forward-compatible with an error-fact layer later. Chosen over error-fact-at-engine-funnel (heavier, M4-level) and silent-skip-Go-parity (invisible failures contradict robustness=visibility). PROTOCOL-LEVEL: loops-go must implement the same rule + counter; vectors should include bool, numeric-string, and missing-_ts cases. Implemented in atoms/engine.py (_is_number/_reject), pinned by libs/atoms/tests/test_fold_rejection.py.
practice/reroute-log-sweep-reconcile                                tail   1   0  2026-06-12  ADOPTED 2026-06-12 (Kyle ratified, same conversation as the thread): three-tier capture-and-review. (1) REROUTE LOG — zero-ceremony one-liner into the existing log kind (collect 20) at the moment of routing around anything; no naming/status/fold-key, which is precisely what makes it fire against flow pressure. (2) SWEEP — fast cadence, every session wrap, before the seal: scan session log entries, promote repeat patterns to friction with proper ceremony, update thread statuses, emit the session arc. Name chosen over 'retro' (baggage): the sweep precedes the seal, fits the vocabulary. (3) RECONCILE — slow cadence, own scheduled sessions (weekly-ish): reconcile lens + friction backlog + stale threads + structural fit; promoted to first-class work. Pricing rationale: silent-reroute cost is an externality (local flow saving, global later cost) — fix by making capture cheaper than the reroute, not by discipline. MECHANISM: Stop hook .claude/hooks/turn-capture.py backstops in-the-moment noticing (the thing that demonstrably fails) — fires the capture question once per substantive turn (>=3 tool calls), stop_hook_active-guarded, conversational turns exempt. Runbook updated (CLAUDE.md Principles + Review cadence section). Escalation path if log under-captures: siftd revival — transcript reading surfaces reroutes without agent cooperation.
design/authorship-vs-delegation-layering                            tail   1   0  2026-06-12  Each principal mints their own fact-signing key; delegation is NOT encoded in fact signatures. Kyle's lean, confirmed 2026-06-12 at live keygen (kyle + kyle/loops-claude on project and identity). Rationale: the fact signature makes exactly one claim — authorship of content (identity domain). On-behalf-of is a second claim (authority domain) with its own primitive: act-chains / OBO / endorsements, vouch's L4 territory. Folding delegation into the signature is the write-receipt temptation again — thickening a primitive to carry a claim it cannot make honestly; the carve-out rule says add a separate primitive when the combined claim is live. Forward-compatible: observer name kyle/loops-claude NAMES the delegation by convention today; the future act-chain ATTESTS what the slash only spells — nothing to migrate, layers compose on stable per-principal authorship. Custody honesty: same-machine keys mean organizational not adversarial separation; kyle's signature currently attests 'session that could load kyle's key' until his custody moves to him (vouch custody story).

design/count-before-budget-ordering                                 tail   1   0  2026-06-28  S4 transform order is filter->select->count->budget (count BEFORE budget). count() emits one row per group in count-desc order with salience=count; a following budget(limit=N) then takes the top-N GROUPS by count (the sort|uniq -c|sort|head semantic). Budget-first would count only the salient head of the raw population and the count-row salience would never do its job — an internal say/do gap (I set salience=count deliberately but the original order never used it). implementation/search-scopes-fts-to-present-kinds                   tail   1   0  2026-06-28  S5 self-review catch: vertex_search returns facts across ALL indexed kinds, ignoring a --kind filter (which only narrowed the post-fetch surface, not vertex_search's view). substrate-friction/peer-assertion-relation              mid     1   3  2026-05-13  resolved · Open (2026-05-13): vouch's Peer/Grant exercise (~/Code/vouch explore/peer-grant subtask, commit d95d36a) surfaced a structural finding — voucher has no slot on Peer because Peer is per-agent (identity+accumulated-authorization-at-current-time) while vouching is per-assertion (voucher×holder×scope). Two recast options proposed by scrivener's worker: (a) engine grows a Vouch atom that names voucher×holder×scope; (b) substrate stays minimal, consumers walk the Fact ledger for the relation. Disposition: (b) — minimal, no engine change. Rationale: assertions live on Facts (observer carries voucher, payload carries scope, chain_metadata carries ancestry); 'who vouched for holder X' is structurally a ledger query, not a field lookup. Walking the ledger isn't workaround, it's the trust-attaches-to-facts model operationalized. Adding a Vouch atom would be substrate-feels-universal — promoting one consumer's relation to engine identity when the existing Fact already carries it. Canonical query: loops fact-history --kind vouch --holder X. Friction stays in the consumer (vouch wraps); engine stays clean. The vouch-impl-handoff Peer/Grant recast question closes via this thread: no recast needed for the voucher×holder×scope relation.

painted-run-cli-args-seam                               mid     2   2  2026-06-15  resolved · RESOLVED by painted 0.3.0 (committed 8518b3c loops-side). Painted answered the seam NOT with my proposed CliContext.args / fetch(ctx), but with a different blessed idiom: HelpArg + run_cli(help_args=[...]) — 'for commands that pre-parse their own args before calling run_cli, describe them so they appear in --help'. So the command keeps its inherent pre-parse (needed for values + branching anyway), fetch closes over the parsed namespace directly, and help_args makes painted's --help list them. trace-diff-rendering-shape                              mid     1   2  2026-05-16  open · Phase 4 design question surfaced by advisor pre-Phase-4 review. Original plan said --diff renders 'field-delta lines like status: open → refined' — that's CUMULATIVE diff (each fact framed against prior state). But DETAILED zoom already shows each fact's payload fields under that fact (per-fact 'patch view' — because fold-merge means the payload IS the patch). So the question is which shape --diff adds value over DETAILED. Two shapes:  (a) PER-FACT (already in DETAILED): each emit's payload-as-fields shown directly. Free, no replay needed. 'What did this emit say' — direct from store.    Example: fact 2 shows: status=refined, refs=A,B,C  (b) CUMULATIVE (advisor's reading of original plan): each fact framed against accumulated prior state. Needs replay-and-compare. 'What CHANGED from prior'.    Example: fact 2 shows: status: open → refined, refs: +C (added)  If (a) is the goal, --diff dissolves into DETAILED+ already exists. If (b) is the goal, --diff is its own thing — replay-and-compare logic, semantics for adds/removes on refs, omitted-fields handling. The lineage-view-missing friction wants (b) — 'the braid through resolution' is about deltas, not snapshots. Phase 4 should commit to (b) explicitly, OR document that (a) suffices and mark friction:lineage-view-missing partial-resolution. Picks up: this thread + sample of how a multi-fact lifecycle would render in each shape at SUMMARY/DETAILED zoom.

daemon-as-new-lib                                       mid     1   1  2026-04-28  parked · Surfaced 2026-04-27 as the operational consequence of paradigm/boundary-as-watcher-triple: drivers as first-class need a host that runs continuously. The daemon isn't 'just a new lib' — it's the operational layer the conceptual work has been implying. What it dissolves (compounding gains): uv-install-on-every-emit (thin clients hit a socket, daemon eats install cost once); vertex program cache (load once, fold in memory, replay never re-runs per emit; per-fact cost ms not seconds); notify/wake substrate (something has to be alive to receive wakes — the daemon is that something); cross-process boundary deduplication (single fire-decider, no race on evaluate_boundaries catchup); sync further attenuation (cadence drivers run continuously in daemon; CLI 'loops sync' becomes 'fire all due cadences now' debug affordance); streaming subscription model becomes natural; today's dispatcher injection carries forward unchanged — dispatcher lives in daemon, fires subprocesses from daemon's process tree. What goes in the lib: process lifecycle (start/stop/status, foreground/background), transport (UDS for v1, length-prefixed JSON), protocol (fact-emit, query, subscribe, fire-driver, list-vertices), vertex registry, driver host loop, dispatcher with subprocess lifecycle, optional event bus for subscribers. What stays where: engine still owns Vertex/Loop/VertexProgram/drivers as primitives — no daemon awareness; atoms unchanged; apps/loops CLI grows thin-client mode (if daemon up, send fact over socket; otherwise direct path). Naming candidates: hearth (always-on warmth, where loops live), keep (preservation + fortified position), roost (where things settle), tend (caretaker), pulse (driver heartbeat), weave (multi-driver coordination), host (accurate but generic). Lean: hearth or keep. Considerations — subprocess management (zombie reaping, output handling), hot reload (defer to v2), single-instance enforcement (PID file or socket-binding), daemon-as-observer (emits own start/stop/dispatched-runs/error facts; same observer-as-vertex pattern), migration path (opt-in initially, fall back to direct if daemon absent — same code two paths). Prior art Kyle flagged for UX mining: siftd (operational persistence patterns, daemon already exists and survives sessions), the recorder lib (just-built, has patterns relevant here), lldap-invite (UX pattern source). Rich-in-refs note: this thread sits at the convergence of comms-vertex-real-time, uv-install-on-every-emit, manual-tick-emission, loop-as-primitive, the dispatch-consolidation work, and the boundary-as-watcher-triple paradigm decision — picking it up will likely surface more refs as those threads converge through the daemon as the substrate. Parked deliberately for later; not blocking, but the ops/cleanliness frame and the next paradigm work both pass through here.

error-handling-and-exception-hierarchy                  mid     1   1  2026-06-14  open · Kyle (2026-06-14): take a deeper look at our exception hierarchy and how we do error handling around it. Triggered by the reanchor bug — operator-facing refusals (resolve_store_path "No store configured", reanchor "requires a .vertex target", engine "no signing key — refusing partial re-anchor", absent .db) are raised as plain ValueError/FileNotFoundError and, with no catch between the _run_* functions and main(), escape as raw tracebacks despite carrying excellent actionable messages. The reanchor fix is LOCALIZED: a catch of (ValueError, FileNotFoundError) at the store view boundary (cli/views/store.py) renders them clean. That is a point patch, not a convention. The systemic questions: (1) should loops have a small exception taxonomy — e.g. an OperatorError/UserError base meaning "expected refusal, render clean + exit nonzero" vs everything else "genuine bug, let it traceback" — rather than catching concrete builtin types per view? (2) where does the catch belong — per-view boundary, the dispatch tiers in cli/app.py, or a single top-level wrapper in main()? (3) the legacy _run_* shims raise and print via painted.show directly while the IR views use ctx.reporter — error rendering is split across both surfaces; unify on the reporter? Hold the earned-granularity line: don't build a hierarchy ahead of need — first audit how many distinct "expected refusal" sites exist across the CLI and whether they cluster.

trace-view-diff-header-and-dead-branch                  mid     1   1  2026-06-16  open · COHERENCE FINDING (2026-06-15, surfaced during step7 golden coverage). trace_view header is unconditionally 'diff <kind>/<key>' (trace.py:48), and the non-diff branch (line 81 else -> stream_view delegation) is effectively DEAD in production: fetch_trace's ONLY caller (fold.py:284) always sets data['_diff']=True immediately after fetch. So _trace ⟹ _diff in production; trace_view is only ever reached in diff mode. Two clean-ups available: (a) DISSOLVE — remove the dead non-diff branch + the zoom!=diff delegation, since it's unreachable (dissolution-test: the branch is a property of a state that's never constructed); OR (b) make non-diff trace a REAL mode (sl read kind/key WITHOUT --diff renders lifecycle records, only --diff renders deltas) — gives the 'diff' header an honest non-diff sibling 'trace'/'lifecycle'. Pick (b) if entity-lifecycle-without-diff is a wanted view; pick (a) if --diff is the only entity view. Golden test_trace_lifecycle currently locks the synthetic non-diff output (header still says 'diff') as a regression net. NOT blocking; belongs with fold-scoping or a read-path cleanup pass.
verify-strip-vs-presigning-detection                    mid     1   1  2026-06-27  open · Disclosure-grammar item c, deferred 2026-06-26 (Kyle's call): the 'keyed observer(s) with no signed facts' + 'no tick is signed' tripwires currently render WARNING for BOTH the benign pre-signing-era store AND a malicious live-edge signature strip — they look identical in the report, so neither INFO (under-alarms a real strip) nor WARNING (cries wolf on the common benign case) is honest. The real fix needs per-observer benign-vs-live-edge distinction in verify_facts/verify_chain reports (engine change): does the unsigned observer's data sit entirely pre-signing-epoch (benign → INFO) or include live-edge facts after signing opened (suspicious → WARNING)? transport-era-signing-key-flow                          tail    1   0  2026-06-14  open · Forward problem flagged by Kyle 2026-06-14 while ratifying the tick-signing floor (decision:design/tick-signing-era-is-a-floor): the SSH "key is always local" assumption that makes signing low-friction breaks in the transport era. Refinement that surfaced: what gets "passed around" is PUBLIC keys (verification), never PRIVATE keys (signing) — SSH all the way down, the private half never leaves the machine. Public-key distribution is largely already designed in the vouch / agent-attestation substrate (JWKS topology, IssuerRegistry dispatch by iss, issuer->namespace mapping) and in the .vertex observers{} registry. The genuinely-NEW problem is CHAIN RECONCILIATION ON MERGE: when store B ingests signed facts from store A (sqlmerge), B's tick chain must absorb A's signed facts WITHOUT (a) re-signing them — that erases A's authorship — or (b) minting an unsigned merge-boundary tick — the Gate-B floor forbids that. So: who mints and signs the boundary tick over a merged window, with what authority, and how does B's era-monotonicity hold across a merge of two independently-signed chains? This is where the tick-signing floor gets its teeth in the multi-store world. Connects to sqlmerge (libs/store transport), Peer/Grant, and the deferred verify-on-receive consumer that reactivates fact-signing enforcement.
rebirth-keyless-attestation-drop                        tail    1   0  2026-06-14  open · OPEN posture question surfaced by review #2 (and named in rebirth.py's floor-exemption comment). "loops store rebirth" with no tick_signer mints an UNSIGNED genesis tick — silently dropping a signed source lineage's attestation. This is NOT a floor bypass: rebirth starts a fresh chain (pre-era, verify ok=True), and the CLI does print "genesis tick unsigned". But it is asymmetric with reanchor, which REFUSES without a key ("a signed fact must not lose authorship"). QUESTION: should keyless rebirth of a SIGNED source likewise refuse (or require an explicit --allow-unsigned), or is silently starting a fresh unsigned lineage the correct posture for a migration/rebirth? Turns on whether rebirth means "continue this lineage" (-> refuse, like reanchor) or "fork a new custody context" (-> unsigned start is fine). Connects to the tick-signing floor (fresh-lineage exemption) and the reanchor refusal precedent.

era-opening-as-protocol-pattern                         tail    1   0  2026-07-02  open · Three instances of one pattern now exist: chain era, signature era (both SPEC §8.5), and the new pre-lineage era (§9.2 genesis-over-existing-store migration). Live-fire trace 2026-04-27 confirmed _fire_live_boundaries (vertex.py:440-504) and evaluate_boundaries (vertex.py:696-802) share IDENTICAL gating logic — same kind check, same match check, same conditions check; only differ in fact source (live: just-arrived fact; catchup: iteration over period_facts from store). Duplication is mechanical not conceptual. evaluate_boundaries' actual job is replay-suppression catchup — facts loaded via replay() with _replaying=True bypass live-fire; evaluate_boundaries re-runs the gates on them once after replay. Belongs in load_vertex_program after vertex.replay(), not in program.sync. Live-fire is complete for every boundary type that exists today: every boundary requires a triggering kind, live-fire fires whenever that kind arrives and the gates (match, conditions) pass. Bonus finding: state-crossing boundaries (fire on fold predicate true regardless of triggering kind) don't exist today and would be the only boundary type requiring evaluation-on-every-state-change. Surfaced as a fourth potential category, then dissolved with the other three into the watcher-triple primitive.  tail   1   0  2026-04-28
Session 2026-04-27 traced an arc-pattern worth naming: small concrete coherence fix (dispatch consolidation, ~80 lines) opened a deeper coherence question (asymmetry between emit and sync), which opened a paradigm gap (time as first-class but never built), which opened a categorization dissolution (boundary-as-watcher-triple as gripping hand), which surfaced an operational substrate question (daemon as where loops actually live). Each step was only visible after the previous landed. Methodology marker: when a coherence fix points at a deeper question, follow it — the path tends to converge on a substrate the conceptual work was implying without naming. The dispatch consolidation shipped at the start turned out to be the right primitive for the daemon parked at the end: program._dispatch_tick is universal across drivers, accidentally built the right shape for the future work. Pattern: small-fix → reframe → substrate. Worth recognizing when it starts.                                                                                                                                                                      tail   1   0  2026-04-28

ulid-regressed-to-uuid4-in-sqlite-store                 high   3   6  2026-05-17  resolved · RESOLVED 2026-05-16 via commits 0a0e64a (substrate fix) + 2a82065 (coherence pass). What landed: (1) engine._gen_id now uses str(ULID()) from python-ulid — pure-Python, no dlopen, restores time-sortable + within-ms-monotonic properties; (2) engine and store schemas drop the dead DEFAULT (ulid()) — every INSERT supplies id explicitly; (3) sqlite-ulid dep dropped from engine/store/top-level pyproject (15 transitive packages removed); (4) all five libs/store test fixtures (test_merge/compact/transport/slice/receive) replaced sqlite_ulid.load+DEFAULT with python-ulid at INSERT — they now mirror production schema and id-supply path. REGRESSION BARS added: engine/test_sqlite_store.py TestIdGenerationContract (3 tests asserting ULID format, within-store id-order matches emission order, cross-store id-order interleaves chronologically); store/test_merge.py TestMergeViaProductionEmitPath (3 tests exercising merge through SqliteStore.append() rather than sqlite_ulid fixtures). These close the structural test-gap that hid the 2026-03-15 regression for two months. AUDIT REVISIONS from agent-traced damage assessment: (a) merge dedup was NOT actually broken under uuid4 — slice preserves id, INSERT OR IGNORE works on either id scheme; the real damage was ORDER BY id semantics (random vs chronological); (b) the 2026-03-15 perf rationale was wrong about cost — 0.5ms was dlopen, not id gen; python-ulid avoids dlopen entirely AND is faster per id than uuid4 (2.3μs vs 2.8μs); (c) rowid was the accidental save that preserved single-store ordering through the regression — captured separately as observation:architecture/rowid-is-load-bearing-for-single-store-ordering. DEFERRED: the 2026-03-15 to 2026-05-16 uuid4 wedge in existing stores. New emits restore the property going forward; pre-Mar-15 ULIDs and post-fix ULIDs share format; the uuid4 wedge stands out as a discrete era. Question of whether to rewrite wedge ids parked — default position is leave-as-historical-fact (rewriting feels like falsification), but Kyle's call. Test count: 2274 passing (atoms 406 + engine 752 + store 60 + loops 1056) — same as pre-fix count, no test removed.

no-daemon-shaped-store-access                           high   1   5  2026-07-16  open · ticked (loops-tasks) runs a 2s-poll daemon over a vertex, but every engine touchpoint is CLI-shaped: load_vertex_program does KDL parse + pin-verify + compile + FULL-history replay per emit, and vertex_read replays per read. root-pyproject-dep-mirror-gap                           mid    1   2  2026-06-14  open · The repo ships as a FLAT vendored wheel: root pyproject (strange-loops) bundles every libs/*/src via hatchling and does NOT depend on the workspace members — so root [project].dependencies must mirror the UNION of all vendored libs' third-party deps BY HAND. A dep added to a lib (engine's rfc8785, added with the JCS migration c1f50ed) is invisible to `uv tool install .` until it is also added to root. `uv run --package` masks the gap because it resolves the workspace env, not the flat wheel. SYMPTOM today: `uv tool install . -e --reinstall` uninstalled rfc8785 (it had survived only as a leftover from the 2026-06-12 ceremony's ad-hoc install) → every `sl` command died with "ModuleNotFoundError: No module named 'rfc8785'" at engine import. FIXED: added rfc8785>=0.1.4 to root pyproject with a comment documenting the mirror requirement; sl restored, verified. RESIDUAL (why this stays open): the gap is structural and SILENT — nothing enforces root ⊇ union(libs); the next lib-dep addition reintroduces it, caught only on a fresh tool install. Candidate fixes: (a) a check diffing root deps vs the lib union, wired into ./dev check; (b) make root actually depend on the workspace members instead of vendoring source; (c) dissolve via lib consolidation (thread:lib-consolidation-reconsider — this friction IS the tax). Reinforces the standing anchor that installed-sl is the production path and the workspace-runner form masks staleness.

loops-skill-cite-syntax-wrong                           mid    1   2  2026-06-29  resolved · The now-global loops skill documented cite as `sl cite <vertex> kind:key ...` — WRONG, and it bit me on the first real cite this session: cite has NO vertex positional (it is dissolved into emit; all positionals are refs), so `project` became a stray ref and the cite landed in the cwd-inferred vertex (not project) with every decision ref dropped. CORRECT forms: vertex-first `sl <vertex> cite REF REF -m` (targets a named vertex, sets ctx.vertex_path) OR cwd-local `sl cite REF REF -m` (from a vertex dir). fts-search-declaration-not-retroactive                  mid    2   1  2026-07-11  open · [ref correction only, message unchanged] Declaring a new 'search' field on a kind in a .vertex file does NOT retroactively index that kind's existing facts. _ensure_fts (vertex_reader.py) advances fts_state.last_rowid monotonically and skips kinds without a search declaration AT THE TIME their rowid is scanned -- once last_rowid passes a fact, it is never re-considered even if search gets declared for its kind later. Hit live 2026-07-11: adding search to decision/thread/task/plan/session/log/cite/hypothesis/friction/observation/seal in .loops/project.vertex (previously only 'design' declared search) left --match returning 0 results on 2948 pre-existing facts until facts_fts + fts_state were manually dropped to force a full rebuild. Contrast with typed-edges, which is genuinely retroactive because it's a read-time overlay, not a write-time indexing cursor -- the FTS mechanism looks like the same kind of late-bound declaration but silently is not. No 'sl store reindex' verb exists to do this safely/discoverably (had to hand-drop tables via sqlite3 directly). Fix-shape: (a) a 'sl store reindex <vertex>' verb that drops+rebuilds facts_fts/fts_state (small, matches the add-verb-gap-boundary-and-preview pattern -- machinery exists, just no CLI surface); (b) at minimum, Window.unindexed or a receipt-time WARN should flag 'this kind now declares search but has N pre-declaration facts not yet indexed' so the gap is visible instead of silently returning zero matches. Every vertex that adds a search declaration to an already-populated kind hits this.

no-conditional-emit                                     mid    1   2  2026-07-14  open · Entity-upsert consumers need a conditional emit (CAS): ticked's runner reaps dead workers by upserting work status=finished outcome=error, but between its fold read and the emit the worker may emit finished/replied — the later error upsert wins unconditionally. ticked shrinks the window by re-reading the run immediately before reaping, but a real fix is engine-level: receive(fact, expect={field: value}) that refuses when the current folded value diverges (same shape as SqliteStore.absorb_edit's expected_head CAS). vertex-first-dispatch-legacy-complexity                 mid    1   1  2026-06-29  open · Vertex-first dispatch (tier 3: sl <vertex> <verb>) is convenience-era complexity from when the CLI was small (Kyle 2026-06-29) — removing it is a CORRECTNESS + SIMPLIFICATION win and dissolves the cite-syntax asymmetry at its ROOT (friction:loops-skill-cite-syntax-wrong was the symptom). It bundles TWO jobs: (1) bare implicit-read `sl project`->read (high-value shorthand); (2) vertex-first OP `sl project cite`/`sl reading add` (legacy duplication of verb-first). Job 2 is the friction: emit takes the vertex AFTER the verb (sl emit <vertex>) but cite has no vertex slot, so vertex-first was the ONLY way to target a vertex with cite -> two grammars, one asymmetry, easy to mis-document. REMOVING tier-3 deletes the bulk of app.py intricacy: _vertex_first, _identify_op_token (op-past-global-flags), _is_predicate_token, the _peel_observer before/after-op split, VERTEX_OPS + population-op argv reconstruction. CORRECTNESS: one grammar per verb; eliminates the "is arg0 a vertex or unknown command?" class (a vertex named like a verb cannot shadow it). REQUIRED COMPANION: verbs take the vertex UNIFORMLY as a positional — cite gains a vertex arg (sl cite <vertex> REF), consistent with emit — a grammar that cannot be mis-stated, the structural fix vs a doc patch. OPEN DECISION (shapes the work): fate of bare implicit-read sl project->read — (a) keep it as a narrow rule + reserve verb names (verb wins on collision), removing only the op form; or (b) full uniformity sl <verb> <vertex> everywhere, zero arg0 ambiguity but sl project->sl read project. Automation already uses verb-first (low migration risk, grep of hooks/config clean); the human-facing change is the implicit-read shorthand. Design+build deserves its own focused session (touches the live dispatch every agent + hook uses).

merge-preflight-dirt-check-path-blind                   mid    1   1  2026-07-16  open · Dogfooding fix/delta-emits, escalation 2: squash_merge refuses to ff a checked-out base when the checkout has ANY uncommitted changes — but the dirt here (.serena/ deletions, unrelated WIP) does not intersect the merge paths, and git's own merge --ff-only handles non-overlapping dirt fine. The machinery's is_dirty gate is path-blind and stricter than git, so task completion is hostage to unrelated checkout hygiene — the common case, since main is usually checked out with something in flight. Why: blanket cleanliness is the conservative read of 'never rewrite a working tree', but it conflates 'would be rewritten' with 'exists'. Fix-shape: intersect dirty paths with the squash's changed paths and only block on overlap (or attempt ff-only and surface git's own refusal). cli-emit-bypassed-engine-gen-id                         tail   1   0  2026-05-17  resolved · Discovered and resolved 2026-05-17. Kyle noticed receipts in this session were still UUID4 despite the ULID engine fix landing yesterday (commits 0a0e64a + 2a82065). Root cause: apps/loops/src/loops/commands/emit.py had its own _new_fact_id() helper returning str(uuid.uuid4()), passed via id_override to the store — bypassing engine.sqlite_store._gen_id() entirely. The docstring even said 'Mirrors sqlite_store._gen_id' — divergence baked in by design. Why pre-generate at all: the receipt needs the id BEFORE vertex.receive() returns (which yields a Tick, not the fact_id), so emit threads a pre-generated id through receive(id_override=). The pattern is sound; the implementation drifted. THIS IS THE SAME BUG CLASS as pattern/exercising-catches-coherence-gaps — feature works in path A (engine.SqliteStore.append() generates ULID when no override), silently broken in path B (CLI emit always provides an override, and that override was uuid4). The existing TestIdGenerationContract in libs/engine/tests/test_sqlite_store.py only exercised the store-direct path; nothing exercised the CLI emit path's id format. FIX: dissolved the duplicate. (1) Renamed engine.sqlite_store._gen_id → gen_id (public). (2) Added gen_id to engine __all__ and lazy imports — single source of truth, accessible as 'from engine import gen_id'. (3) Dropped _new_fact_id() and 'import uuid' from emit.py; emit now uses 'from engine import gen_id' then fact_id = gen_id(). (4) Added test_receipt_id_is_ulid_format to apps/loops/tests/test_emit_receipt.py — locks the format invariant at the emit-path level so a future swap fails fast there, not just at the store layer. Verified end-to-end: 'sl emit ...' now produces receipts like '01KRTA5282726QWX88TKGR635P' (26-char Crockford ULID, no hyphens). 1869/1869 tests pass across loops + engine + store. Discovered via in-session smell — Kyle asked 'why are we still seeing UUIDs?' after reinstalling via 'uv tool install . -e'. implementation/reanchor-verify-not-divergent                              mid    1   4  2026-06-14  Investigated the smoke-test's HIGH candidate-bug "verify-vs-reanchor opposite verdict on identical bytes" (from observation:design/disclosure-grammar-smoke-test-catalog). VERDICT: not an integrity-verb divergence. Three confirmations on properly-keyed stores: (1) verify and reanchor AGREE on a keyed copy of the current store, and reanchor is BYTE-IDEMPOTENT — the db sha256 is unchanged after "96 facts re-signed, 8 ticks re-chained" because ed25519 is deterministic, so re-signing canonical bytes reproduces identical signatures; (2) reanchor with private keys absent raises BEFORE any write (post-sha == pre-sha) — the engine explicitly guards "refusing partial re-anchor; a signed fact must not lose authorship"; (3) the JCS swap (c1f50ed) is a no-op for existing ASCII/integer payloads — compact-sorted JSON already equals RFC 8785 for that content, which is why reanchor changed zero bytes and why even the pre-JCS archive still verifies chain-intact. The "opposite verdict" reduces to: verify succeeds while reanchor's no-key / no-vertex REFUSAL rendered as a raw Python traceback (uncaught ValueError) — read as a crash / contradicting verdict. Both refusals carry excellent messages; they were just not caught at the CLI boundary. FIX LANDED: catch (ValueError, FileNotFoundError) at the store view boundary (apps/loops/src/loops/cli/views/store.py), render via reporter.err + exit 1; other exception types still raise so genuine bugs stay debuggable. 3 regression tests + full app suite green (1322 passed). This is the first TIER-1 disclosure-honesty fix and it de-risks the broader pass: verify's GREEN is honest about chain-integrity — only the signature-disclosure grammar (checkmark-vs-attested, the backwards warning, covered-vs-signed) still needs work.
design/curation-belongs-in-surface-not-renderers                          mid    1   4  2026-06-29  Audit verdict (w6d4zptvv, 37 agents): Surface IS the renderer-invariant fixed point -- an invariance probe proved context (is_tty/zoom/width/mode/format) does NOT leak into Surface construction; --json was byte-identical (md5 0601dcfd) across pipe, COLUMNS 80 and 400, and -q/-v/-vv. So the umwelt-fork is NOT a no-common-reality problem; it is that the renderers RE-CURATE the shared Surface behind its back. The fold lens applies salience reorder plus namespace windowing as its BASE projection while to_dict emits surface.rows verbatim -- two different curations of one Surface, neither announcing which it holds. Reframe / dissolution: promote curation OUT of the renderers and INTO Surface as a declared, serialized budget (Window provenance), computed once and emitted in --json. Then every renderer collapses to render(Surface, context) with zero independent loss, the umwelt-difference between any two views becomes a computable Window-diff, and the aggressive curation a human-orient redesign needs is done ONCE with provenance and is one in-band keystroke from reversal. The constraint is not add-instrumentation; it is stop-the-renderers-from-curating, let-Surface-own-it. Grow-the-substrate over fork-the-consumer.

practice/cross-adapter-review-catches-real-issues                         mid    1   2  2026-05-13  Observation (2026-05-13): cross-adapter review pipeline (claude-opus plan+impl, codex/gpt-5.5/low review on fresh session via subtask) produced two real Important findings on libs/sign carve first review pass that same-session continue would have missed. The fresh-session discipline forces re-derivation from PLAN+diff, not continuation of the implementer's reasoning. Verdict: when stakes warrant (security surface, cross-repo coordination), the cross-adapter pipeline earns its overhead. Pattern: claude plan + claude impl + codex review on critical paths.
atoms/refs-are-vocabulary-not-fact-shape                                  mid    1   2  2026-05-13  Self-correction surfaced 2026-05-13 #vouch-impl (scrivener catch, msg 1613 § B). Fact dataclass slots are (kind, ts, payload, observer, origin) — confirmed at libs/atoms/src/atoms/fact.py. No refs field on Fact. Refs land at payload._refs (vertex_reader.py:984 does d.pop('_refs', ()) separating them from semantic payload at read time). My msg-1612 framing of 'refs as substrate primitive' was imprecise; sharper framing: refs-as-vocabulary IS the substrate primitive (the convention of payload-level pointers + emit-time resolution + entity-ref graph index); refs-as-Fact-shape would be premature substrate. Substrate-deferred verdict gets stronger. Practice note: when reasoning about substrate primitives, distinguish 'a slot on the dataclass' from 'a vocabulary convention with substrate support.' Refs are the latter. Reply at message 1614.
pattern/declaration-vs-call-site-discriminator                            mid    1   2  2026-05-19  Discriminator for "declare per-kind on the loop block" vs "universal CLI feature": does each consumer of the field-role need per-kind variability? preview YES (friction:status+message, decision:message, change:empty — visible heterogeneity). search YES (different kinds index different fields). prose-as-stdin-eligibility NO — the kind does not decide; the user at the call site does, by writing the flag at emit time. paradigm/robustness-as-failure-metabolism                                 mid    2   1  2026-06-10  REFINED by Kyle in-conversation: the visibility of failures IS the robustness — not a byproduct of metabolism but the property itself. Metabolism without visibility would be silent absorption, exactly the failure mode the system exists to kill (April's silent hook-rot is the type specimen). Hierarchy: visibility is the property, metabolism is the mechanism, signing is the guarantee that visibility survives the parties who witnessed it. A failure you can see is fixable; a failure that is signed has trustable history. Original framing and counterweight (n=1 survival counts, mechanism-robust-before-track-record) stand.

implementation/signing-enforcement-status                                 mid    1   2  2026-06-13  CODE-CONFIRMED (2026-06-13 smoke-test): fact-signing at emit is OPPORTUNISTIC, not required; verification is AUDIT-ONLY. emit always composes fact_signer_for(path) into the vertex program; a fact signs iff keys/ exists AND the emitting observer has a key (keys/<observer>/ or flat self-key) AND store is in signing era — else appends UNSIGNED silently (no warn, no refusal). NO vertex 'require signature' config exists: the only lang 'strict' flag refuses on emit VALIDATION failures (undeclared kind/observer via validate_emit), NOT on missing signatures. fact_verifier_for/verify_chain are called ONLY in commands/store.py (store verify + reanchor) — operator-invoked, registry-aware (each fact sig checked against its declared observer key exactly). vertex.py receive, program.py, sync.py do NOT verify. Net: sign-if-you-can on write + check-if-you-ask on demand; neither required-on-emit nor verified-on-receive. The progressive-policy + sign-on-emit-verify-on-receive design specified the require+verify layer; it is NOT implemented. NUANCE: require-on-emit is a present gap and the ROOT of the disclosure over-claim (verify renders signed/✓ as an enforced guarantee for an unenforced property). verify-on-receive is correctly DEFERRED not missing — no untrusted cross-store receive path exists yet (local single-writer; verifying your own just-signed fact is circular); load-bearing at the transport/peer era. Kyle's recollection confirmed: the 'vertex must require it' layer is the missing precondition for signing to matter.
implementation/seal-no-era-guard-silent-unsigned                          mid    1   2  2026-06-14  Catalog candidate-bug #2 ("seal mints unsigned tick reporting success; seal never discloses its signing outcome") investigated on keyed vs no-keys copies. BOTH claims CONFIRMED — and this is the ONE REAL finding of the candidate-bug sweep (the HIGH verify-vs-reanchor, FC-04 read-path, F8 ticks-UTF-8, and the reanchor traceback all dissolved / downgraded / fixed). (b) DISCLOSURE: sl seal prints "tick: project (13 fields)" + "stored: seal/..." and NEVER states whether it signed — the output is BYTE-IDENTICAL whether the tick was signed (keyed copy) or not (no-keys copy). The "13 fields" is no signal: the signature COLUMN exists in both, just NULL when unsigned. (a) INTEGRITY (worse than the catalog's "likely harmless artifact"): on a store already in the signed era, sl seal run WITHOUT keys mints an UNSIGNED tick, exit 0, success output — and that unsigned tick BREAKS THE CHAIN: store verify then reports "✗ CHAIN BROKEN ... unsigned tick after signed era — signature stripped or era regressed". Airtight via the symmetric control: the keyed copy's seal minted a SIGNED tick (9/9 signed, chain intact); only the no-keys seal breaks it. ASYMMETRY with reanchor: reanchor GUARDS this exact boundary ("refusing partial re-anchor; a signed fact must not lose authorship") and refuses without keys; seal does NOT — it is the one verb that can silently CREATE the era-regressed / chain-broken state that verify is designed to detect. Contradicts the tick-side STRUCTURAL-signing posture (ticks are vertex-self-signed at a single funnel, "structural from this point forward" — unlike opportunistic per-observer fact signing). REAL-WORLD REACH: the SessionEnd hook runs sl seal automatically on every session close; if keys are ever absent/moved at close (fresh clone pre-keygen, copied store, relocated keydir) the hook silently breaks the chain and nothing says so until a later store verify. Design call held for Kyle — see thread:seal-era-boundary-guard.

design/umwelt-fork-no-shared-reality                                      mid    1   2  2026-06-29  The same read renders a materially different reality depending on output context. Human-on-TTY sees width-clipped truncated styled output; agent-on-pipe sees the full plain render. Kyle's framing: the umwelt has no common reality to share a view of. finding/low-budget-non-monotonic-bounce                                   mid    1   1  2026-05-11  Watch-for, not finding: E5 replication (run 13) shows slight non-monotonicity at the lowest budgets — B=140 persist_frac=0.17, B=95 persist_frac=0.22, B=60 persist_frac=0.22. convergence/participatory-not-authenticative-three-sites                  mid    1   1  2026-05-13  Observation (2026-05-13): the 'verification at boundaries, not at fact-shape' position has prior commitment in loops AND convergent framing at three sites. (1) STRANGE-LOOPS.md commits: 'paradigm is participatory (observer-as-stance), not authenticative (proof-of-origin).' Trust attaches to accumulated stream, not to per-fact signatures. (2) alcove's trust-topology essay: 'the audit trail IS the trust system.' Same framing. (3) siftd's provenance model: 'who pushed this data' (audit trail) rather than 'cryptographic proof of source authenticity.' Same. Three independent sites taking the same position is structural evidence the substrate stance is right. Fact-signing as engine primitive would contradict this position — it would make the substrate authenticative rather than participatory. Implication: engine ships nothing for fact-signing. Consumers that need durable cryptographic signatures (vouch today, others if they arise) put signatures in consumer payload and verify in their vertex policy. Substrate stays participatory; consumers add authenticative layer where their use case demands it.

design/rebirth-ref-rewrite-dissolves                                      mid    1   1  2026-06-10  Ref-rewrite component of rebirth dissolves: payload refs are stored entity-keyed (kind:key), resolved to fact ids at READ time (resolve_entity_id), so id migration needs no payload rewriting. Raw old ids appear only in prose messages (32/2048 facts in project.db) — history, not structure; rewriting would falsify quotes. Old tick envelopes re-enter as tick-facts VERBATIM (signature must verify against original bytes); old-to-new id mapping stays recomputable because the migration transform is deterministic: new_id = ULID(ms(fact.ts) || sha256(old_id)[:10]). Determinism is what makes receipt-verification-by-re-run an operation rather than a promise.
ops/three-id-eras-in-stores                                               mid    1   1  2026-06-10  Live rebirth of project.db surfaced a THIRD id era: 919 lowercase ULIDs (sqlite-ulid C-extension era) alongside 872 uuid4 ids and ~258 canonical python-ulid ids. Lowercase sorts above uppercase in ASCII, so the lowercase era is ALSO order-broken — 01kjtv... sorts after every 01KTQP... forever. The mixed-era story was always told as two eras; the itch was one number reading wrong (1791 ids migrated vs the 872 the story predicted). ulid-migration needs no change: the canonical-form rule (uppercase Crockford or re-mint) covers all three eras uniformly — one rule in the receipt, not three.
paradigm/rejected-counter-is-state-about-folding                          mid    1   1  2026-06-12  The {target}_rejected counter is a new ontological category in fold state: the first state key the engine writes that no fact supplied and no fold op declared — state ABOUT the folding, not folded state. Same family as Avg's hidden _sum/_count, but those are implementation detail of a declared op; _rejected is the engine commenting on the quality of its own input stream. If this category grows (parse-rejection counts? grant-rejection counts? boundary-misfire counts?), it wants a naming convention and a place in the tick envelope — observability of the fold process itself, which connects directly to robustness-as-visibility-of-failures. Noted, not prescribed; second instance earns the design.
practice/adversarial-review-catches-what-confidence-misses                mid    1   1  2026-06-14  Two-round adversarial review (Workflow, 15 agents each) of the seal-era-guard arc caught TWO real holes that solo confidence missed — after I had said "pretty confident we're good." Round 1 (on 9f2de91, verb-scoped guard): HIGH — the guard sat on the seal VERB, but "sl emit <v> seal" fires the same boundary via cmd_emit, a one-token bypass of the floor. A store-level invariant cannot be enforced at the verb. Round 2 (on 6c368e4, after moving the guard to the engine mint): MEDIUM — Vertex._store_tick is NOT the only live mint (apps/tasks' harness emit_tick is a second), so enforce_floor=False was fail-OPEN; a forgotten caller silently bypassed the invariant. Both fixes were dissolutions the reviews named: (1) move enforcement from the verb to the store mint; (2) flip the default to fail-SAFE (enforce by default, name the exemptions). PATTERN for a security/integrity invariant: (a) enforce at the single lowest chokepoint, not at each call site; (b) make enforcement the DEFAULT with named opt-outs, never opt-in — both "where" and "default polarity" are load-bearing, and adversarial review surfaced them precisely because the holes were the cases my framing assumed away ("single mint point", "covers the hook"). One refinement of the review itself: checking append_tick's callers BEFORE applying the reviewer's literal "guard in append_tick" caught that it is shared with rebirth/slice — the right seam was narrower than the review's first suggestion. Review informs; caller-analysis decides placement.

design/two-pre-build-risks-surface                                        mid    1   1  2026-06-27  Stress-test surfaced two risks to resolve BEFORE building the Surface keystone (2026-06-27): (1) GRANULARITY-BY-CARDINALITY -- the integration auto-returns the whole body when a filtered read collapses to one row, making output SHAPE depend on result-set size (a read that returns a body today returns headlines tomorrow when a second fact lands). Breaks the load-bearing addressed-read=body trust -> agents reroute to sqlite again. Fix: make whole an explicit address property, not a runtime row-count side effect. (2) FTS CONFIRM ASYMMETRY -- the read/write symmetry (emit re-enters the read seam) is FALSE on the search axis: a just-emitted fact is unsearchable via --match until re-index, so emit->read --match->nothing-landed->panic->sqlite manufactures the exact reroute were eliminating. lens-dissolution-pattern                                                  tail   1   0  2026-03-07  The lens system resists elaboration in the generic layer. Seven threads dissolved when the answer shifted from 'make the generic handle this' to 'write a custom lens.' The identity prompt was a domain lens pretending to be generic infrastructure — moving it to config/lenses/ was escalation, not construction. The lens-escalation-path investigation itself dissolved into 'confirm it works + write docs.' The meta-pattern: when you try to elaborate the generic, the system tells you to escalate instead. Domain logic belongs in domain lenses; the generic should be simple, not smart. retrospective-observation-pattern                                         tail   1   0  2026-03-07  The loops system started with live sources — shell commands that observe the present. df -h reports disk NOW. Discord polls messages NOW. All sources implicitly assumed ts ≈ now. Siftd introduces retrospective observation — the conversations already happened, the files already exist, the source observes the past. This forces three concerns apart that were conflated when all sources were live: (1) Event time (ts) — when the thing happened, source-provided; (2) Store time (ULID) — when the store received it, system-provided; (3) Source cursor — what the source has already observed, source-managed. For live sources all three converge. For retrospective sources they diverge. The general principle: a source is a lens on the external world. It decides what to observe (cursor), knows when things happened (event time), and the system records when the observation arrived (store time). The _ts override, source cursors, and the rowid/ts query split are all consequences of this single distinction. The paradigm already supports it — 'facts are observations of what occurred' does not require 'what occurred' to be simultaneous with the observation.
format-as-lens-dissolution                                                tail   1   0  2026-03-07  Kyle identified that --format ndjson is a point solution for what lenses solve generally. NDJSON output is a lens, not a format. This dissolves the entire format layer into lens selection. The pandoc analogy: any input shape can be rendered through any output lens. The implementation architecture needs this plumbed in — it's not a CLI feature, it's a rendering architecture realization. Current --json flag is already a lens wearing format's clothing.
parse-intake-asymmetry                                                    tail   1   0  2026-03-08  The vertex has declarative transformation on output (fold for aggregation, lens for display) but none on intake. Parse exists in atoms with 10 ops and KDL syntax in .loop files, but it runs at Source collect time — before the Fact reaches the vertex. Vertex.receive() goes straight to store.append() with no transformation step. This means sources must know about vertex indexing needs (which fields FTS5 wants). The fix: vertex-level parse declarations on kind blocks, applied at receive() before store. Source parse (raw→structured) and vertex parse (structured→enriched) compose as two stages. The .vertex file becomes the single declarative surface for intake shaping, aggregation, indexing, and rendering.

practice/lens-wider-than-named-principle                                  tail   1   0  2026-05-11  The deliberation-depth lens (named for 'suspicious-cleanness-as-overfit-check') measures something wider than its name: low-experimental-deliberation, which captures THREE epistemic kinds — TYPE A (confirmed-by-code-reading, solid), TYPE B (confirmed-by-first-test-that-fit-too-well, scrutinize), TYPE C (confirmed-by-reasoning-alone, latent). pattern/cross-repo-consumer-runtime-contract                              tail   1   0  2026-05-14  Cumulative meta-pattern surfaced 2026-05-13 across four vouch friction exercises (vouch HEAD 49565b6; docs/friction/{peer-grant-exercise,issue-vouch-write-path,service-shell-exercise,rescission-write-path}.md). After four exercises of sustained external implementation pressure on the loops substrate from vouch (first cross-repo consumer), a coherent cumulative pattern: ZERO substrate changes pushed, SIX consumer-side disciplines accumulated, SEVEN substrate framings crystallized. The disciplines-list IS the consumer-runtime contract surface — not a TODO list of substrate fixes. **The six disciplines (substrate-doesn't-enforce list):** (a) body-supplied voucher/ttl_seconds/rescinder silently ignored — forward-auth identity is canonical; (b) no widening primitives (engine.grant/expand_grant) in write-path modules — AST-walk test enforces across app.py/policy.py/forward_auth.py/rescission.py; (c) normalize scope to frozenset before constructing Peer/Grant, or only use lattice helpers (delegate/restrict/grant_of/restrict_grant) which coerce; (d) walk Fact chains explicitly to recover voucher relation — substrate provides refs+store, traversal lives in policy; (5) construct Peer only from trusted (anchor) provenance — Peer(...) construction appears only in policy.py:resolve_voucher gated by forward-auth; (6) call rescind_vouch only from a caller that has looked up the target and authorized the rescinder — rescind_vouch is thin substrate append, lookup-and-authorize lives in VouchPolicy.rescind. **Disciplines move from documented → test-pinned where AST-checkable.** (b) is fully AST-enforced; (5) is enforced by structural fact (single call site); (6) is documented + test-pinned via test_rescinder_observer_independent_of_target_voucher demonstrating the substrate refuses to enforce it. **The seven substrate framings:** (1) substrate-feels-universal trap — named in peer-grant-exercise summary; did not fire across four exercises despite multiple candidate moments; (2) refs-as-vocabulary not refs-as-Fact-shape — Fact has 5 slots (kind/ts/payload/observer/origin), refs are payload._refs vocabulary convention with emit-time resolution, not a dataclass field; (3) runtime-model assumption-leak — loops substrate shaped under single-threaded CLI assumptions, first concurrent consumer surfaces latent assumptions (SqliteStore thread-affinity Obs 2); (4) substrate-types-and-wire-types parallel-projected from same substrate slot — Fact.ts:float, JWT exp:int, rescission receipt ts:int; consumer projects per its protocol; (5) capability-projecting vs identity-asserting writes — auth forward-looking (current state) vs backward-looking (historical state); issuance vs rescission canonical; generalizes to permission systems, trust networks, claim issuance/withdrawal, attestation/recantation; (6) kind_subtype-vs-peer-kind three-signal rule — kind_subtype right shape only when subtypes share payload-shape AND auth-shape AND write-semantics; one signal of divergence qualifies for peer-kind promotion; (7) the substrate-doesn't-enforce list IS the consumer-runtime contract surface — meta-framing that reframes the list from TODO to contract; growth there is healthy, misreading as TODO would gradually pull legitimate consumer-discipline INTO substrate via fix-the-TODO pressure. **Convergence-from-different-vantages happened reliably across six peer-exchange cycles** (msgs 1599-1616): scrivener at consumer, loops-claude at substrate, landing on the same verdict from opposite sides. Evidence the substrate is real — not just internally consistent but consistent under sustained external implementation pressure from a different vantage. **For the next cross-repo consumer:** this artifact is the registry to read FIRST. Same shape will recur. Most frictions resolve into consumer-side disciplines, not substrate changes. The substrate-feels-universal trap is the failure mode to watch for — when a property feels universal because the substrate is universal, apply the discriminating question 'is there a second consumer with concrete divergent constraints needing this TODAY?' (N=2 bar). The substrate-doesn't-enforce list grows monotonically; that's healthy. **For the substrate side:** the participatory-not-authenticative stance (ADR-0001 §Trust attaches to the assertion, alcove's trust-topology essay, the-substrate-that-doesnt-decide essay) is now operationalized — substrate refuses to encode runtime-shaped invariants, consumer's runtime owns them. The discipline list is the operational form of that stance. Future-me/future-consumer: when reaching to add substrate enforcement for a discipline on this list, the burden of proof is high: name the second consumer with concrete divergent constraints, name the substrate primitive that lifts cleanly, and confirm the discipline can't continue to live at the consumer.
pattern/validation-axis-kind-vs-status                                    tail   1   0  2026-05-16  Same axis (provisional vs validated) encoded two ways by two designs. InferiorMinion: split across kinds (decision pre-validation, pattern post-validation). Ours: status-lifecycle on single kind (hypothesis status=proposed -> confirmed -> refined). Kind-split is LOUDER at read-path — kind itself carries validation state, no status field read needed. Status-lifecycle is more flexible — one kind covers whole arc, easier to track refinement. Not a correctness question; a which-property-do-you-want-louder question. Hold as architectural alternative.
pattern/staleness-utility-decay-vs-attention-decay                        tail   1   0  2026-05-16  Two staleness models from two designs. InferiorMinion: pattern is stale when no decision/insight has ref-d it recently (utility-decay — useful-but-unused). Ours (reconcile lens): thread is stale when not touched this session (attention-decay — open-but-unvisited). Different signals, both real. Utility-decay needs ref-graph traversal over recent tick window; attention-decay needs session-touch timestamps. Worth considering whether reconcile lens should expose both axes.
peer/exchange-as-metabolic-catalyst                                       tail   1   0  2026-05-16  Sharpening the peer-exchange model from session 2026-05-16. InferiorMinion design doc was catalyst for runbook design, but the runbook is genuinely ours not theirs: feature= became feature=+ops=; their friction-queue became our friction-kind; their validation-via-kind illuminated by contrast our validation-via-status. Pattern: peer exchanges do NOT propagate substrate — they propagate IDEAS that the receiving substrate METABOLIZES into its own shape. This is distinct from "convergence" (which suggests two substrates arriving at same form) and distinct from "adoption" (which suggests taking the form whole). Metabolism preserves the receiving substrate s grain while integrating the external idea. Predicts: peer exchanges produce most value when the receiving substrate has enough structure to metabolize against. Without that structure, ideas pass through unchanged (adoption) or fail to integrate (rejection). With it, ideas emerge transformed into substrate-native form.

architecture/slash-overload-as-system-notation-gap                        tail   1   0  2026-05-20  At least six distinct conceptual meanings on / in the codebase: (1) kind/key entity address (CLI input), (2) kind/key payload value scanned by auto-resolver, (3) namespace/topic fold-key prefix (today's bug site), (4) parent/scope observer hierarchy (engine/observer.py), (5) template/subdir vertex template (init.py), (6) parent/alias combine child (resolve.py:_resolve_vertex_for_dispatch). Each consumer chose / organically because it's the obvious separator; the collision came from accumulation not design. Filesystem solved this with one meaning (hierarchy); URIs solved it with reserved chars per role (scheme: path/ ?query #fragment). Loops drifted into multi-meaning slash without picking either strategy. The non-decision IS the structural gap — not the resolver's behavior specifically, but the absence of a chosen notation methodology. Adjacent to but distinct from typed-refs question: even with typed addresses, the / character still does five other things in the codebase that occasionally collide.
pattern/auto-resolver-coherent-until-trace-split-it                       tail   1   0  2026-05-20  Timeline grounding 2026-05-19: the auto-resolver was internally coherent from 2026-03-09 (39d8de9) introduction through 2026-05-15. Slash-form on both write (_resolve_entity_refs) and read (no walker existed yet — _ref siblings WERE the navigation mechanism). The convention split was created in 2026-05-16 by the trace verb commit (803ba03) — cross-kind ref walking needed unambiguous parsing, chose colon over slash, fixed the read parser (_parse_fact_refs introduced as colon-only), did not propagate to write side. Same commit message explicitly notes catching 'ref parser used / separator instead of : (refs are kind:key)' — the team thought the bug was caught when only the read side was fixed. Reframes 'messy codebase' as 'deferred-completion debt from a 3-day-old multi-step refactor.' This is a normal failure mode of substantial refactors (sweep gap), not a discipline collapse. Useful as orienting context whenever the typed-refs work is picked up — the convention drift has a specific origin commit and a specific deferred sweep, not ambient cruft.

implementation/incumbent-bugs-surfaced-by-go-oracle                       tail   1   0  2026-06-03  The Go oracle surfaced real protocol-vs-impl divergences LIVE in THIS monorepo Python (libs/atoms, libs/engine) — all fix-BOTH, i.e. our code has them too. Actionable here independent of loops-go (verified vs HEAD 33937f6). Inventory: (1) replay reads ORDER BY rowid (store_reader.py:207, sqlite_store.py:179/207/223) + merge regenerates rowid in scan order (merge.py:74) => merge(A,B) != merge(B,A) for Collect/Window/Upsert; fix = replay in (ts,id) order. (2) _make_latest falls back to time.time() when _ts absent (engine.py:38) => determinism violation; fix = errors-are-facts. (3) resolve_entity_id ORDER BY rowid DESC LIMIT 1 (store_reader.py:235) => ref-time-blind AND merge-UNSTABLE; fix = ts-bounded (ts,id) resolution. (4) bool folds as 1 — Python bool-is-int, no guard: Sum(true)=1, Min/Max=True (engine.py:53/164/176) => would violate a normative true!=1. (5) Sum/Avg/Min/Max/TopN-by omit num() guard => TypeError on non-numeric field (Go silently returns 0/skip — different failure modes). (6) silent-false condition coercion: </> return False silently on non-numeric target (vertex.py:57-93) => a boundary like cpu>80 against a string-typed cpu never fires, no diagnostic. The monorepo backlog the port found; whether/when WE fix these in Python is a separate call from the loops-go protocol forks.

implementation/read-path-attestation-neutral                              tail   1   0  2026-06-14  FC-04 from observation:design/disclosure-grammar-smoke-test-catalog ("read-path green over broken-signature fact") investigated on a keyed copy. VERDICT: the everyday read/fold path is attestation-NEUTRAL, not attestation-GREEN. Method: tampered a signed fact's payload on a keyed copy. store verify flags it loudly (✗ FACT SIGNATURES BROKEN, names the exact fact: "signature invalid — content does not match the observer's authorship signature"); the read/fold path renders the tampered content verbatim ("message: TAMPERED CONTENT") at every zoom including -vv FULL, with NO attestation glyph — headline identical to a clean fact. The render path is signature-BLIND by construction: lenses/fold.py + commands/fetch.py never inspect per-fact signatures (the only attestation-aware code is the TICK-window/witness-era path used by --ticks; "by-fold signature" in fetch.py is the fold-shape sense, not crypto). So the catalog framing is slightly imprecise: there is no false GREEN — read simply does not speak to attestation at all, UNLIKE store verify's green ✓ which DOES claim ok (that is the real overstatement surface, captured separately as the TIER-1 checkmark fix). CONCLUSION: not a behavioral bug; reframes as a disclosure-DESIGN question — should the everyday read path carry a tamper/unsigned marker, or is attestation-as-a-separate-verb (read = content view, verify = integrity view) the honest separation that keeps crypto out of every read? Same gating as enforcement: with no untrusted receive path yet (decision:design/fact-signing-enforcement-deferred), a read-path tamper-marker has no consumer — it reactivates when something can write facts you did not author. Held for Kyle as a TIER-1 design call, not a fix. Second catalog candidate-bug to dissolve under the same method as the HIGH (observation:implementation/reanchor-verify-not-divergent).

design/orient-salience-is-distinct-from-read-salience                     tail   1   0  2026-06-28  Salience-FF map surfaced the crux answer in EVIDENCE: orient ranking != read ranking, and Surface only materializes the read one. All 3 session-open lenses (session_start, session_landing, identity_prompt) are ORIENT surfaces; the in-repo fold lens is the READ drill-in and windows PURELY by salience (n+inbound). The orient lenses structurally CANNOT rank on salience alone — each OVERLAYS a time signal salience does not carry: identity_prompt _recency_boost (+2<3d/+1<14d/0/-1>90d) and session_landing focus-marks (added/updated/cited/stale = what-changed/what-needs-me). Neither has a Surface analogue. So Surface.salience = n+inbound = IMPORTANCE, timeless = a READ salience; ORIENT needs importance + recency + change-state. Implication for thread:human-umwelt-static-view: the human static view is NOT read-styled-with-salience; orient is a richer ranking the Surface should materialize as first-class (recency + change-marks), instead of each orient lens bolting it on by hand divergently. The salience FF is the structural prerequisite that exposes this gap.

implementation/replay-swap-was-per-vertex                                 tail   1   0  2026-07-17  MAJOR pre-existing engine bug found by the receipt-change adversarial review (not caused by the diff — the lens question 'can receive_receipt run with a store attached during replay?' surfaced it): Vertex.replay swapped only the ROOT's _store to None, so parent replay forwarded historical facts to nested children whose stores were still attached — a stored child re-appended the parent's ENTIRE history on every load (1→2→3 rows per replay, reproduced empirically by the verify agent). Same discipline hole: no try/finally on the swap, so a raising fold mid-replay left _store=None permanently (close() silent no-op, handle leaked, boundaries dead). Fixed fdda675: _replay_guard context manager makes the swap per-TREE (walks _children recursively, saves/restores store+replaying flags in finally). Side effect worth knowing: child boundaries no longer fire mid-replay — matches replay's own documented contract ('without re-appending or firing boundaries') and prevents double-folding; the old behavior was the bug wearing a feature's shape. CALIBRATION: my own pre-check read replay() and concluded 'clean — every path nulls _store before replaying'; TRUE per-vertex, FALSE per-tree. I verified the discipline at the wrong scope. The structural sensor (workflow lens + empirical repro) caught what my targeted read did not — the read confirmed the claim I brought to it.

Horizon (read-side visibility) is enforced NOWHERE. Pure transform, same pattern as limit/last/salience_window.  3. Scope -- FOLD VIEW ONLY (current-state default read). --facts (event/lifecycle history) stays faithful always -- different read axis, and corpus audits (this session's friction audit ran on --facts + --json to verify status transitions) need the untouched history regardless of what the fold view curates.  4. Uniform across encoders -- the hide runs in the Surface budget stage, before text and --json rendering diverge, so both channels see the identical cut (satisfies the invariance constraint Decision B already proved: query-keyed is allowed, channel-keyed is not).  5. Defeat -- --all shows everything (reusing the vocabulary docs/dev/umwelt-divergence-and-curation-in-surface-2026-06-28.md already picked for in-band windowing defeat, one vocabulary for all budget-cuts). An explicit status= predicate in the same read auto-disables the default hide for that read (asking for status=resolved while hiding resolved would be incoherent).  6. Provenance -- Window gets an honest limited_by="status" + shown/total counts, same no-silent-caps discipline as every other budget cut.  First concrete instance: friction { hide status="resolved" } in .loops/project.vertex, once implemented.  Touches: libs/lang/loader.py (grammar), apps/loops/src/loops/surface.py (budget()), apps/loops/src/loops/cli/operation.py + dispatch.py (wiring), .loops/project.vertex (declaration), tests.  Deferred to its own implementation session per Kyle's 2026-07-11 call -- this fact captures the shape so that session starts from a settled mechanism, not a blank page.
architecture/bulk-emit-ndjson                     tail   1   0  2026-07-12  proposed · Design entry for the top consumer ask (2026-07-12 homelab-audit retrospective). Shape: sl emit --ndjson FILE|- accepting fact-per-line, with (1) strict PREFLIGHT over the whole batch before any write (all-or-nothing option), (2) ONE signed batch receipt, (3) SYMBOLIC intra-batch IDs so forward references resolve within the batch — this dissolves the manual topological ordering strict typed edges currently force (audit had to emit a project before its feature, then re-emit), (4) the batch file doubles as the durable, replayable import manifest the audit found missing (payloads exist only in the append-only db + session JSONL today). Design inputs to hold: the sync engine already consumes ndjson — check dissolution into that path before building a parallel one; interaction with feat/internal-table _decl reservation (a batch touching declarations must respect write-time reservation semantics from S1/S2 — design these aware of each other); batch receipt vs per-fact receipts is a write-receipt question (receipt = your batch at instant T, one tick-eligible unit?); decide whether a failed preflight names ALL violations or first (audit ergonomics say all). Elevated from friction:no-bulk-emit-for-interactive-use (N=1 speculative 2026-07-03) by cross-vendor consumer demand.
architecture/payload-constraints-in-declarations  tail   1   0  2026-07-12  proposed · Sequencing position (2026-07-12): the homelab-audit consumer wants semantic payload constraints in vertex declarations — required fields, enums, lifecycle defaults — plus a validate surface covering folded state (loops validate --store --refs --foreign-refs). The need is real (Sol validated status vocabularies, feature lifecycle fields, and foreign fact pins in ~custom Python because loops validate only checks declaration syntax), and it is a DIFFERENT AXIS from strict mode (strict = ref resolution + kind declaration at emit; constraints = payload validity). Position: design this AS PART OF the store-canonical declaration schema after internal-table S3+ lands, not as KDL ingress surface now — the internal table is exactly where constraint declarations would live and be historized, and designing them into the ingress format mid-migration would double the absorption surface. The bulk-emit preflight (design:architecture/bulk-emit-ndjson) is the natural first consumer of a constraint engine — batch validation wants machine-checkable payload rules. Related existing ask: friction:emit-automation-via-vertex-def (default field values, e.g. status defaults open) is the smallest member of this family and should fold into the same design rather than ship separately.
